INTRODUCTORY NOTE

THIS Upani·π£ad has derived its name from the six Pra≈õnas or questions it contains. It belongs to the Atharvaveda and is probably of the PippalƒÅda≈õakhƒÅ. ≈öa·πÖkara calls it a BrƒÅhma·πáa complementary to the Mantra Upani·π£ad, i.e. the Mu·πádaka, which also belongs to the same Veda. There are six chapters in the Upani·π£ad, and each begins with a question. The first question refers to the origin of the created beings, the second to the constituents of the human personality, the third to the nature and origin of PrƒÅ·πáa; the fourth is about the psychological aspect of the human personality, the fifth about Pra·πáava, and the sixth about the metaphysical principle in man. Like the Taittirƒ´yopani·π£ad, it also takes the reader gradually from the gross to the subtle principles of life, revealing one by one all the folds of Matter that enwrap the ƒÄtman. Moreover, in this Upani·π£ad alone we find a clear mention being made of the creation originating from Matter and Energy.

NOTE ON TRANSLITERATION

IN this book DevanƒÅgarƒ´ characters are transliterated according to the scheme adopted by the International Congress of Orientalists at Athens in 1912 and since then generally acknowledged to be the only rational and satisfactory one. In it the inconsistencyirregularity and redundancy of English spelling are ruled out: f, q, w, x and z are not called to use; one fixed value is given to each letter. Hence a, e, i and g always represent ‡§Ö, ‡§è, ‡§á and ‡§ó‡•ç respectively and never ‡§è, ‡§á, ‡§êand ‡§ú‡•ç or other values which they have in English; t and d are always used for ‡§§‡•ç and ‡§¶‡•ç only. One tialde, one accent, four macrons and ten dots (2 above, 8 below) are used to represent adequately and correctly all Sanskrit letters. The letter C alone represents ‡§ö‡•ç. Since the natural function of h will be to make the agho·π£a gho·π£a (e.g. kh, ch, ·π≠h, th, ph, gh, jh, ·∏çh, dh, bh), it would be an anomaly for a scientific scheme to use it in combinations like ch and sh for giving ‡§ö‡•ç and ‡§∑‡•ç values; hence ch here is ‡§õ‡•ç and sh ‡§∏‡•ç ‡§π‡•ç. The vowel ‡•† is represented by ·πõ because ri, legitimate for ‡§∞‡§øonly, is out of place, and the singular ·πõi is an altogether objectionable distortion. The tialde over n represents ‡§û‡•ç, √±. Accent mark over s gives, ‡§∂≈õ; dots above m and n give anusvƒÅra (<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734946641Screenshot2024-12-23150629.png"/>), ·πÅ and ‡§ô‡•ç ·πÖ, respectively. Dots below h and r give visarga (:), ·∏•, and ‡•†, ·πõ, respectively. Dots below s, n, t and d give their corresponding cerebrals ‡§∑‡•ç, ‡§£‡•ç, ‡§ü‡•ç and ‡§ô‡•ç, ·π£. ·πá, ·π≠and ·∏ç ; and macrons over a, i, u and ·πõgive ƒÅ, ƒ´, ≈´, ·πù respectively. Macrons are not used to lengthen the quantity of e and o, because they always have the long quantity in Sanskrit. Sanskrit words are capitalized only where special distinctiveness is called for, as in the opening of a sentence, title of books, etc. The scheme of transliteration in full is as follows:

‡§Ö a ‡§Ü ƒÅ, ‡§á i, ‡§à ƒ´, ‡§â u ‡§ä ≈´, ‡§ã ·πõ, ‡§ã ·πù, ‡§è e, ‡§ì o, ‡§êai, ‡§îau,<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1734946641Screenshot2024-12-23150629.png"/>·πÅ,**:**·∏•, ‡§ï‡•ç k, ‡§ñ‡•ç kh, ‡§ó‡•ç g, ‡§ò‡•çgh, ‡§ô‡•ç ·πÖ, ‡§ö‡•ç c, ‡§õ‡•ç ch, ‡§ú‡•ç j, ‡§ù jh, ‡§û‡•ç √±, ‡§ü‡•ç·π≠ ‡§† ·π≠h, ‡§°‡•ç ·∏ç, ‡§¢‡•ç·∏çh, ‡§£ ·πá, ‡§§‡•çt, ‡§•th, ‡§¶‡•ç d, ‡§ß‡•çdh, ‡§®‡•ç n , ‡§™‡•ç p, ‡§´‡•ç ph, ‡§¨‡•ç b, ‡§≠‡•çbh, ‡§Æ‡•ç m, ‡§Ø‡•ç y, ‡§∞‡•ç r, ‡§≤‡•ç l, ‡§µ‡•ç v, ‡§∂‡•ç ≈õ, ‡§∑ ·π£, ‡§∏‡•ç s, ‡§π‡•ç h.

PEACE INVOCATION

‡•ê ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•Å‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§É ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ú‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡•à‡§∞‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•à‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§µ‡§æÍ£≥ ‡§∏‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•Ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•á‡§Æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É‡••
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§® ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∑‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§®‡•á‡§Æ‡§ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§®‡•ã ‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•Å‡••

‡•ê ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§ ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§ ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••

** ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§É** O gods (or worshipful Ones ) ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡•á‡§≠‡§ø‡§É with the ears (of the teacher and the disciple) ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•çwhat is auspicious (i.e. words of the scripture etc.) ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•Å‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ may we hear. ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§É efficient to sacrifice (‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç we) ‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§≠‡§ø‡§É with eyes ‡§≠‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•çwhat is auspicious (sacrifice, worship, etc.) ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§Æ may we behold. ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§ø‡§∞‡•à‡§É perfect (lit. firm) ‡§Ö‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡•à‡§É limbs and organs ‡§§‡§®‡•Ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§É bodies (‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç we having) ‡§§‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§É singing (your praise) ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç allotted by the Lord ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É span of life ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•á‡§Æ may we obtain fully. ‡§µ‡•É‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§æ‡§É He who is glorified in the scriptures by ancient preceptors ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Éthe Supreme Lord ‡§®‡§Éfor us ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§øprosperity (in our study and in the practice

of what is learned) ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•Å may confer. ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§æ‡§É all-knowing ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∑‡§æP≈´·π£an (lit. he who nourishes the world) ‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•Å may confer on us prosperity ‡§Ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§®‡•á‡§Æ‡§ø‡§É he who protects from harm ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Éthe celestial Bird ‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•Å may confer on us prosperity. ‡§¨‡•É‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É the Lord of Prayers (‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§™‡§æ‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø taking care of our spiritual lustre ) ‡§®‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•Å may confer on us prosperity.

Om. O worshipful Ones, may our ears hear what is auspicious. May we, efficient to worship, see with our eyes what is auspicious. May we, who sing your praise, live our allotted span of life in perfect health and strength.

May Indra, the Lord who is extolled in the scriptures, P≈´·π£an the all-knowing, TƒÅrk·π£ya who saves from all harm, and B·πõhaspati who protects our spiritual lustre, vouchsafe us prosperity in our study of the scriptures and the practice of the truths contained therein.

Om Peace : Peace : Peace.

[NOTES‚Äî These two Peace Invocations are mantras that originally occur in the ·πögveda Sa·πÅhitƒÅ (1. lxxxix. 8. 6), and are used in connection with the Upani·π£ads of the Atharvaveda].

PRA≈öNOPANI·π¢AD

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§É FIRST QUESTION

** ‡•ê ‡§®‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡•á‡•§ ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§É ‡•ê‡•• ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ú‡§É, ‡§∂‡•à‡§¨‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É, ‡§∏‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡•Ä ‡§ö ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É, ‡§ï‡•å‡§∏‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ã, ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§µ‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§ï‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§π‡•à‡§§‡•á ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§æ, ‡§è‡§µ ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø, ‡§§‡•á ‡§π ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§™‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§É‡••‡•ß‡••**

** ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ú‡§É** Son of BharadvƒÅja ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§æ (called) Suke≈õas ‡§ö and, ‡§∂‡•à‡§¨‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É son of Sibi ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É(called) SatyakƒÅma ‡§ö and, ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É of the clan of Garga ‡§∏‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡•Ä the grandson of S≈´rya ‡§ö and, ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§É the son of A≈õvala ‡§ï‡•å‡§∏‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É (called) Kausalya ‡§ö and, ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§É of Vidarbha ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§µ‡§É BhƒÅrgava (i.e. born of the clan of Bh·πõgu), ‡§ï‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§É the son of Katya (one whose great-grandfather is still living) ‡§ï‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ä (called) Kabandhin‚Äî‡§§‡•á they ‡§πso the story goes ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§É devoted to Brahman ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§É Stead fast in Brahman ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç the Supreme‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§ÆBrahman ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§∑‡§Æ‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§É seeking (‡§Ü‡§∏‡§®‡•ç were) ‡§§‡•áthey ‡§π indeed

‡§è‡§∑‡§É this person ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à surely ‡§§‡§§‡•ç that ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç all ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø will tell ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus (‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø having thought) ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§£‡§Ø‡§É with sacrificial fuel in hand ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•çthe venerable ‡§™‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§™‡§≤‡§æ‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç PippalƒÅda ‡§â‡§™‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§É approached.

Om, adoration to the Supreme Self. The Supreme Lord who is ever attracting all towards Him is the Highest Reality.

Suke≈õas, the son of BharadwƒÅja; SatyakƒÅma, the son of Sibi; the grandson of S≈´rya of the clan of Garga; Kausalya, the son of A≈õvala, BhƒÅrgava of Vidarbha, Kabandhin, the son of Katya;‚Äî all¬π these were devoted to Brahman and steadfast¬≤ in Brahman, and were in search of the supreme Brahman. With¬≥sacrificial fuel in hand, they approached the venerable PippalƒÅda, thinking that he would tell them all that.

[NOTES‚Äî I*. All these were devoted to Brahman*‚Äî i.e., ‘Brahman’ here means the Sagu·πáabrahman of the Vedas.

    1. Steadfast in Brahman*‚Äîi.e., well established in the practices of devotion to the Sagu·πáabrahman or Hira·πáyagarbha.
  1. With sacrificial fuel in hand‚Äî According to the customary rules, one should not visit the king, the deity in the temple, and the Guru without offering some kind of present. It was also customary with the pupils in

ancient times to get for their teachers the fuel for sacrifices.]

‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§π ‡§∏ ‡§ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‚Äî ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ ‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•, ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§, ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç‡§π ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•®‡••

‡§∏‡§É that ‡§ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§É ·πö·π£i (revealer of some Vedic mantra ) ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç to them ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö said ‡§π verily ‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡§æ by penance, ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£ by abstinence, ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ by faith, ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø‡§É again ‡§è‡§µ indeed ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç a year ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§• live. (‡§Ö‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç after that) ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç according to the desire ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç questions ‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§ may ask; ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø if ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É (we) know ‡§µ‡§É to you ‡§π assuredly ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç all ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É shall tell.

The ·πö·π£i said to them : ‘Live again a year more in penance, abstinence, and faith; then you may ask questions according to your desire; if I know them, assuredly I shall tell everything to you.’

[NOTES‚ÄîThe ≈öruti here clearly indicates by the story that unless the pupil is thoroughly trained and disciplined through Tapas, abstinence, and faith, it is not possible to comprehend subtle spiritual truths. While Tapas and Brahmacarya are helpful in restraining the mind and the senses, ≈öraddhƒÅis needed to make the pupil’s mind receptive to the holy teachings impartedbythe Guru.]

** ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§ï‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ä ‡§ï‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§® ‡§â‡§™‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ, ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡•ã ‡§π ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•©‡••**

‡§Ö‡§• afterwards ‡§ï‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡§¨‡§®‡•ç‡§ß‡•Ä Kabandhin, the young son of Katya, ‡§â‡§™‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Øhaving approached (PippalƒÅda) ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ asked : ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç Venerable Sir, ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É these (visible) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É creatures ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡§É whence ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à as they say ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á are born?

Then KƒÅtyƒÅyana Kabandhin having approached (PippalƒÅda) asked (him): ‘Venerable Sir, whence are these creatures born?’

** ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§∏ ‡§π‡•ã‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‚Äî ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É, ‡§∏ ‡§§‡§™‡•ã‡§Ω‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§, ‡§∏ ‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∏ ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§•‡•Å‡§®‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø, ‡§è‡§§‡•å ‡§Æ‡•á ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•™‡••**

‡§∏‡§É he (PippalƒÅda) ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à to him ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö said : ‡§∏‡§É that ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É Creator ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É (‡§∏‡§®‡•ç) being desirous of creatures ‡§§‡§™‡§É austerities (meditation) ‡§Ö‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ performed ; ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§§‡§™‡§É meditation ‡§§‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ having performed ‡§è‡§§‡•å these two ‡§Æ‡•á my ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É creatures ‡§¨‡§π‡•Å‡§ß‡§æ in manifold way ‡§ï‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§É will do (produced) ‡§á‡§§‡§øthus (‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Øhaving determined) ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç food (Matter) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç PrƒÅ·πáa (Energy) ‡§ö and ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§•‡•Å‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç pair ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•á created.

To him PippalƒÅda replied : ‘The Creator’ desirous of progeny performed austerity in the

form of meditation. Having performed austerity, He created the pair‚Äî Matter¬≤ and Energy‚Äî thinking that they together would manifoldly bring forth creatures for Him.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. Creator‚ÄîHira·πáyagarbha.

  1. Matter and Energy‚Äî According to ≈öa·πÖkarƒÅcƒÅrya Rayi in the text means food, or the Moon; and PrƒÅ·πáa means Fire, or the eater. ≈öa·πÖkara’s interpretation is based upon the Vedic notion that all food is produced by the subtle influence of the Moon which is the cause of the liquid principle or Rasa on the earth; and the Sun which gives the earth its fire-principle or Tejas is the consumer of the former. This is physically as well as physiologically true for life is sustained and multiplied by food and respiration, Anna and PrƒÅ·πáa. We have translated ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§øas Matter and ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£as Energy. Hira·πáyagarbha, the cosmic mind, first created out of himself Matter and Energy which produce all the varieties of the universe. This interpretation is in accord with the discoveries of modern Science, and quite convincing when read with the subsequent passages.]

** ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ã, ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§µ ‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ, ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§µ ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§É‡••‡•´‡••**

‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É the Sun, ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à verily ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É Energy; ‡§ö‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§æ the Moon ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§É Matter ‡§µ‡§æ or ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç what ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç withform (gross) ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç what ‡§ö and ‡§Ö‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç formless (formless (subtle) ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç these ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç all ‡§µ‡•à verily ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§É Matter ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç therefore ‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Éform ‡§è‡§µ indeed ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§ÉMatter.

The¬π Sun is Energy, and Matter¬≤ indeed is the Moon; or, Matter¬≥ verily are all these‚Äîwhat is with form and what is formless; therefore‚Å¥ form is Matter.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. The Sun is Energy.‚ÄîThe Sun being the greatest centre of Energy, it has been conceived of as the main spring of life and activity, and is identified here with the PrƒÅ·πáa, the cosmic Energy.

  1. Matter indeed is the Moon.‚Äî The Moon being devoid of all heat and light, is identified with inert matter; moreover, just as the Moon shines by the light of the Sun, so Matter too expresses itself through force or energy. Probably there is another reason for this identification. The word Rayi means food, and according to the Vedic mythology, the nectar of the Moon is the food of the gods, and on the earth all vegetables are produced through its influence; so the Moon is food or Rayi; but the crudeness of the simile has been cleared in the next sentence.

  2. Matter verily are all these etc.‚Äî Here the ≈öruti hints at the latest scientific view that whatever exists in this universe‚Äîobjects with form or without form, gross or subtle, atomic or compound‚Äî is Matter, that Rayi and PrƒÅ·πáa or Matter and Energy, are mutually convertible, and that the difference between the two is not radical but only conceptual‚Äî a difference only in the states of manifestation.

  3. Therefore form is Matter.‚ÄîBut according to the ordinary conception of matter, it is inert and gross and occupies space, i.e. it has form.]

** ‡§Ö‡§•‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§â‡§¶‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§ö‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§¶‡•Ä‡§ö‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ß‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡••‡•¨‡••**

‡§Ö‡§• now ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É the Sun ‡§â‡§¶‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç having risen ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç when ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç the eastern ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§Æ‡•ç quarter ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡§§‡§ø enters, ‡§§‡•á‡§® by that ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç eastern ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç PrƒÅ·πáas ‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å in the rays ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á holds ; ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç when ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç southern ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç when ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•Ä‡§ö‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç western ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç when ‡§â‡§¶‡•Ä‡§ö‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç northern ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç when ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§É nadir, ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç when ‡§ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç zenith, ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç which ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ intermediate ‡§¶‡§ø‡§∂‡§É quarters, ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç when (‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç else ) ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç all ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø illumines ‡§§‡•á‡§® by that ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç all ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç PrƒÅ·πáas ‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•Å in the rays ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á holds.

Now, when the Sun after having risen enters the East, then he holds PrƒÅ·πáas of the East in his rays. When he illumines the South, the West, the North, the Zenith, the Nadir, the Intermediate quarters, and all, by his rays he holds all the PrƒÅ·πáas.

[NOTES‚Äî The ≈öruti here states that wherever there is the manifestation of life and energy, they are due to the quickening influence of the Sun.]

** ‡§∏ ‡§è‡§∑‡§µ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•É‡§ö‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•≠‡••**

** ‡§∏‡§É** He ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ÉPrƒÅ·πáa ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§É of universal form ‡§µ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§∞‡§É of universal life ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ÉFire ‡§â‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•á rises. ‡§§‡§§‡•ç that ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç this ‡§ã‡§ö‡§æ by the ·πök ‡§Ö‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç described.

Thus¬π rises He the PrƒÅ·πáa, of universal life and universal form, the Fire. It has been described by the following ·πök¬≤.
[NOTES‚Äî 1. Thus rises he etc‚Äî The Sruti asserts that the Sun and Fire are both manifestations of the same PrƒÅ·πáa (Energy) which is universal and all-per-vading.

  1. ·πök.‚Äî A laudatory verse a collection of which constitutes the ·πögveda.]

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§∏‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§§‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§ ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§É ‡§∂‡§§‡§ß‡§æ ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡§∂‡§§‡§ß‡§æ ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑ ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡••‡•Æ‡••

‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§Æ‡•ç of universal form ‡§π‡§∞‡§ø‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç full of rays ‡§ú‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç omniscient ‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç the basis of all (life) ‡§è‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç one ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§É effulgent ‡§§‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç he who gives heat (‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the sun ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡§É ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É the seer know). ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§É of thousand rays ‡§∂‡§§‡§ß‡§æ in hundred ways ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É existing ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç of the creatures ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É life ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É the sun ‡§â‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø rises.

(The wise know him, who is) of universal form, full of rays, omniscient, the basis of all

(life), the effulgent one, and (great) giver of heat. There rises the Sun of thousand rays who is manifold in existence and the life of all creatures.

[NOTES‚Äî The spiritualization of PrƒÅ·πáa identified with the Sun is most significant in the VedƒÅntic Metaphysics.]

** ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É, ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•á ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡§§‡•á, ‡§§‡•á ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ú‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á, ‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§ã‡§∑‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§É‡••‡•Ø‡••**

** ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É** PrajƒÅpati (Lord of the creatures) ‡§µ‡•àverily‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡§∞‡§É the whole year ; ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø his ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§ö the south ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§ö and the north ‡§Ö‡§Ø‡§®‡•á two paths (‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§§ exist) ; ‡§§‡§§‡•ç therefore ‡§Ø‡•á who ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à verily (or, as it is well-known) ‡§§‡§§‡•ç that ‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á(‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§ö) the performance of Vedic sacrifices and doing such philanthropic works as digging a well or a tank for the public, or establishing an almshouse etc., ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç work worth doing, or of permanent value, ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus ‡§â‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á do devoutly ‡§§‡•á they ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç the lunar ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç world ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§ú‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á conquer (attain) ; ‡§§‡•á they ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á return again. ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç therefore ‡§è‡§§‡•á these ‡§ã‡§∑‡§Ø‡§É the ·πö·π£is ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É desirous of progeny, ‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç the southern ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á go ; ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à indeed ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§É Matter ‡§Ø‡§É which ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•É‡§Ø‡§æ‡§£‡§É the path of the manes.

The¬πyear is verily PrajƒÅpati, and his¬≤ paths are two, the southern and the northern ; now, those who perform the I·π£·π≠ƒÅp≈´rta^(3) (Vedic sacrifice and charitable work) thinking them as works of supreme value, they attain the world of the Moon and afterwards return here again. Therefore those ·πö·π£is who desire offspring go by the Southern Path. Matter‚Å¥verily is this path of the manes.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. The year is verily PrajƒÅpati.‚Äî Here ‘year’ means Time. Time indeed is PrajƒÅpati, the Lord of creation, because everything is within the control of time. Moreover, psychologically the conception of time forms the basis of that of creation; for creation is the phenomenon of causation (i.e., a reading of Reality as cause and effect). We cannot conceive of a cause changing into an effect without the necessary conception of moments which alone gives us the idea of antecedence and sequence. ≈öri K·πõi·π£·πáa also says in the Gƒ´tƒÅ ‘Of measurers I am Time.’

  2. I·π£·π≠ƒÅp≈´rta-

** ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§∂‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ ‡§Ü‡§π‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡•á ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§•‡•á‡§Æ‡•á ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§â ‡§™‡§∞‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§∑‡§°‡§∞ ‡§Ü‡§π‡•Å‡§∞‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•ß‡••**

‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç with five feet ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§¶‡§∂‡§æ‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç with twelve forms ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç father ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§Éof the sky ‡§™‡§∞‡•á above ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•á half ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∑‡§ø‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç excreting (giving rains) ‡§Ü‡§π‡•Å‡§É(the sages) say. ‡§Ö‡§• again ‡§™‡§∞‡•á ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á others ‡§á‡§Æ‡•á these (the sages) ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç the seer (the sun) ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•áof seven wheels ‡§∑‡§°‡§∞‡•áon six-spoked (chariot) ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç placed (‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus) ‡§Ü‡§π‡•Å‡§É say.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. He is the father.‚ÄîThe sun is called the father of all because all life proceeds from him and is sustained by him. The sun is identified with the year or Time as he is the maker or measurer of Time.

  1. With five feet‚Äîi.e., with the five seasons, counting Hemanta and ≈öi≈õira as one.

The drift of the text is that it is the Sun, the PrƒÅ·πáa, who makes the time, who marks it out into the year which has several sub-divisions and phases, andwho thus functions as the coutroller and father of all. This verse and occurs originally in the ·πögveda-1. 164. 12]

‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ ‡§ã‡§∑‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤ ‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§∞ ‡§á‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡••‡•ß‡•®‡••
** ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡§É** the month ‡§µ‡•à verily ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É PrajƒÅpati (lord of creatures) ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø its ‡§ï‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡§™‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§É the dark fortnight ‡§è‡§µ only ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§É matter ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡§É the bright (fortnight) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É PrƒÅ·πáa. ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç therefore ‡§è‡§§‡•á these ‡§ã‡§∑‡§Ø‡§É the ·πö·π£is ‡§∂‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§≤‡•á in the bright (fortnight) ‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡•ç sacrifices ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø perform ; ‡§á‡§§‡§∞‡•á others ‡§á‡§§‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç in the other (i.c. in the dark fortnight).

The month is verily PrajƒÅpati. Its dark fortnight is Matter, and its bright fortnight PrƒÅ·πáa. Therefore some ·πö·π£is perform their sacrifices in the bright fortnight; others in the other half.

[NOTES‚ÄîThe same play of light and darkness‚Äîof Matter and Energy‚Äîof activity and inactivity‚Äîwhich is manifest in infinite Time, in the form of creation and dissolution, is noticeable also in the period of a year in two solstices and also in a month in the form of two fortnights, and in a day in the form of day and night.]

** ‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§π‡§∞‡•á‡§µ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§µ ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§É‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•á ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ ‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á, ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•å ‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡••‡•ß‡•©‡••**

‡§Ö‡§π‡•ã‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É Day and Night ‡§µ‡•à surely ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É PrajƒÅpati. ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø its ‡§Ö‡§π‡§É day ‡§è‡§µ indeed ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É PrƒÅ·πáa (Energy)

‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§É night ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§É matter. ‡§Ø‡•á who ‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ by day ‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ in sexual intercourse ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á combine ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§µ‡•à assuredly ‡§è‡§§‡•á they ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§ï‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø dissipate. ‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•å in night ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç when ‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ in sexual intercourse ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á are united ‡§§‡§§‡•ç that ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç control ‡§è‡§µ indeed.

Day and night are PrajƒÅpati; of PrajƒÅpati day is PrƒÅ·πáa (Energy) and night is matter.So those who unite in sexual love by day, dissipate their PrƒÅ·πáa; but¬πcontrol, indeed, is that when they unite by night.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. But control indeed etc.‚Äî We have translated the word Brahmacarya in the text as ‘control’ for it apparently means here ‘discipline,’ or self-control in sexual indulgence, and not complete continence which the word usually means.]

** ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ã ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•™‡••**

** ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç** food ‡§µ‡•à verily ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É PrajƒÅpati; ‡§§‡§§‡§Éfrom that ‡§§‡§§‡•ç that ‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§É the seed (semen) (‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á is produced) ; ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç from that ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É these ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É creatures ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á are born.

Food is verily the PrajƒÅpati. From that is produced the seed, and from that again all these creatures are born.

[NOTES‚Äî This Section directly gives the answer to the first question; but hitherto the ≈öruti has been dealing only with the fundamental principles of creation. The question was ‘Whence are these creatures born?’; and in answer to it, the teacher first said (Sec. 4) that Matter and Energy are the two fundamental principles of creation. Next (Sec. 5 to 8) the various expressions and functions in general, of Energy and Matter, in maintaining the creation are described. Then (Sections 9 and 10) he spoke of the two paths, the material and the spiritual, by which a soul can travel after death, according to his Karma and Knowledge. Next (Sections 11 to 13) he digressed in giving the descriptions of minor sub-divisions of time, such as seasons, months, and days, and pointed out that all these divisions, like Time itself, are but the working of the same Matter and Energy, and through them they control the life. And then in the present Section he gives the direct reply that ‘from the seed the creatures are born.’

It may appear strange why the teacher should apparently depart so much from the point before directly giving the answer which after all was a statement of a simple biogenetic fact perhaps well-known to the questioner himself. But there is a deeper significance in it. In making so many preliminary statements with regard to PrƒÅ·πáa and Rayƒ´ (Energy and Matter) before mem- tioning the Biological origin of life, the teacher had two things in view. First, by stating the fact that Matter and Energy are the principal sources of the Creation, the teacher pointed out that the bioplasmic origin of life is but a secondary expression of the same Matter and Energy. Secondly, by mentioning the

eschatology even before his answer to the question on the origin of life, he hinted that there could be no first origin of life, nor of any creature for the matter of that, in the true sense of the term. Life is beginningless and so are the creatures. The life-principle, the soul, has to undergo bodily expressions from time to time, from Cycle to Cycle,‚Äî that is all,‚Äîbut has no real origin.

In the Sections 9, 12, 13 and 14 the word PrajƒÅpati is used with a peculiar significance. Primarily the word means BrahmƒÅ or Hira·πáyagarbha whose another expression is Time (as explained in the notes on the 9th Section) and then it is used rather loosely for the minor divisions of Time such as year, month, and day, as they consist of the dual expressions of Matter and Energy. In the 14th Section, the sperm is called PrajƒÅpati since it is the source of the individual physical life as Hira·πáyagarbha is that of the collective.]

** ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§•‡•Å‡§®‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§∑ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§™‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•®‡•´‡••**

‡§§‡§§‡•ç thus ‡§Ø‡•á those ‡§§‡§§‡•ç that ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç rule of PrajƒÅpati ‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø observe ‡§§‡•á they ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§•‡•Å‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç a pair ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á produce. ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç of those ‡§§‡§™‡§É penance ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç abstinence, ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å in whom ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç truth ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç established, ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç their ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§É the heaven of BrahmƒÅ.

Therefore, those who observe the¬π rule of. Prajapati produce¬≤ a pair. For them verily

is the Brahmaloka¬≥, who have penance and abstinence‚Å¥ and in whom truth abides.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. The rule of PrajƒÅpati‚Äîi.e. ·πötukƒÅlagamanam, and what is spoken of in section 13.

    1. Produce a pair*‚Äîi.e., son and daughter.

  1. The Brahmaloka‚ÄîHere only the Candraloka is meant and not the supreme heaven of BrahmƒÅ.

  2. Abstinence‚Äîi.e., Brahmacarya mentioned in section 13.

This section tells us that those ignorant householders who simply observe the rule of PrajƒÅpati,’ get the fruit in this world in the shape of sons and daughters,’ but those who have in addition, penance discipline,’ and truthfulness and have performed I·π£tƒÅp≈´rta, go to the ‘Heaven of Moon’ hereafter.]

** ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡•å ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§ú‡•ã ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•ã ‡§® ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ú‡§ø‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§® ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•¨‡••**

** ‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å** in whom ‡§ú‡§ø‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç deceit, ‡§Ö‡§®‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç falsehood, ‡§® not, ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ guile ‡§ö and ‡§® not, ‡§§‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç their ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•å that ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∞‡§ú‡§É pure ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Éthe world of BrahmƒÅ. thus (the section ends).

That pure¬π world of BrahmƒÅ belongs to them only in whom rests not deceit, falsehood, or guile.

[NOTES‚Äî1. Pure world of BrahmƒÅ‚Äîi.e., the supreme heaven spoken of in section 10.]

END OF THE FIRST QUESTION

‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§É SECOND QUESTION

** ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§π‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§µ‡•ã ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•§ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á? ‡§ï‡§§‡§∞ ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á? ‡§ï‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•á‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†? ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡••**

‡§Ö‡§• then ‡§µ‡•à‡§¶‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§É ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡§µ‡§É the BhƒÅrgava of Vidarbha ‡§è‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç him ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ asked, ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç Holy Sir, ‡§ï‡§§‡§ø how many ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§É gods ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç creatures ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á support? maintain. ‡§ï‡§§‡§∞‡•á how many ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç this ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á manifest? ‡§ï‡§É who ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É again ‡§è‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç of these ‡§µ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§É the greatest ?

Next, the BhƒÅrgava of Vidarbha asked him: ‘Holy Sir, how many are the Gods¬π who support the creatures? How many (of them) manifest¬≤ it? And who again is the greatest of them?’

[NOTES‚Äî1. The gods‚Äîi.e., powers, organs, or the senses.

  1. Manifest it‚Äîi.e., express their power.]

** ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§∏ ‡§π‡•ã‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡•ã ‡§π ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§É ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§É ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•§ ‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É‡••**

** ‡§∏** he (PippalƒÅda) ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à to him ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö said, ‡§è‡§∑‡§É that ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É god ‡§Ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§É the sky, ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É air, ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§Éfire, ‡§Ü‡§™‡§É water, ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä earth, ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç speech (organ of speech), ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É mind, ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§É eye, ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ear ‡§ö and ‡§§‡•á they ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø having manifested (their power) ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§¶‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø vaunt ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç we ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç this ‡§¨‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç body (lit perishable) ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø having held together ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É support.

To him he replied : ‘The ether is that God, the air, fire, water, earth, speech, mind, eye and ear. These having manifested their power, vaunt and say, ‚ÄúWe (each of us), holding this body, support it."

** ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£ ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§Æ‡§æ‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§• ‡§Ö‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ß‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§¨‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ; ‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§¨‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ‡•Å‡§É‡••‡•©‡••**

‡§µ‡§∞‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§É the supreme (chief) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É PrƒÅ·πáa (vital energy) ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç to them ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö said ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç self-delusion ‡§Æ‡§æ do not ‡§Ü‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§• fall into‡§Ö‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç I ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç this ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç myself ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ß‡§æ in five parts ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø having divided ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç this ‡§¨‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç body ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø holding ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø support. ‡§§‡•á they (the other gods) ‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§¶‡§ß‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É unbelieving ‡§¨‡§≠‡•Ç‡§µ‡•Å‡§É became.

The chief PrƒÅ·πáa then declared: ‘Do not be deluded. I¬π alone, dividing myself into five

parts, hold this body and support it.’ But they were not disposed to believe his words.

[NOTES‚Äî1. I alone dividing myself etc.‚ÄîHere it refers to the five kinds of vitai breath, viz., PrƒÅ·πáa, ApƒÅna, SamƒÅna, UdƒÅna, and VyƒÅna which are supposed to function in maintaining the body. But the powers which the sensory and motor organs manifest by their functioning are only expressions of the one vital energy that pervades the whole body, and which again is a part of the universal energy. There is only one PrƒÅ·πáa that acts through the body and Nature. This truth has been allegorically described here as well as in the subsequent sections.]

‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§ ‡§á‡§µ; ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡•á‡§§‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§è‡§µ‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§øÍ£≥‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§ï‡§∞‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§µ‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á, ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§øÍ£≥‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§µ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§®‡•ç‡§§, ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§É‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•™‡••

‡§∏‡§É he (PrƒÅ·πáa) ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç from indignation ‡§ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç upward ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•á was going out ‡§á‡§µ as if ; ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç when he i.e. the chief PrƒÅ·πáa) ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§§‡§ø when gone out, ‡§Ö‡§• thereupon ‡§á‡§§‡§∞‡•á others ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§è‡§µ all ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§É PrƒÅ·πáas (senses and organs) ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á get out; ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç when he (te the chief PrƒÅ·πáa) ‡§ö and ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á when being established ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á all ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á are established, ‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æas‡§Æ‡§ß‡•Å‡§ï‡§∞‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç the king of the bees (queen-bee) ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç in

going out ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Éall ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§É bees ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á go out ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç when he (the King) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á being established ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§É ‡§è‡§µ all ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á are established ; ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç thus ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç speech ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É mind ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§Éeyes ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ears ‡§ö and (‡§Ö‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç did). ‡§§‡•á they ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ‡§É being pleased ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç the PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø praises.

He from indignation appeared to go out upwards (from the body); thereupon as he was about to go out, all others seemed to go out and when he was being established, all others were also established. Just as bees go out when their queen goes out, and settle down when she settles down, so did the speech, mind, eye, ears, (etc.). Being satisfied they praised the PrƒÅ·πáa.

[NOTES‚ÄîIt should be noted here that mind also is included among the dependants of PrƒÅ·πáa; i.e., even the mental activities are but the expressions of the same energy that functions through the body and the senses.]

‡§è‡§∑‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑ ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§ò‡§Æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§∑ ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É‡•§
‡§è‡§∑ ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É ‡§∏‡§¶‡§∏‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡••‡•´‡••

‡§è‡§∑‡§É this (PrƒÅ·πáa) ‡§Ö‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§É fire (‡§∏‡§®‡•ç being) ‡§§‡§™‡§§‡§ø burns ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É sun; ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this ‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É cloud (‡§è‡§∑‡§É this) ‡§Æ‡§ò‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç Indra ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É wind ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É bright

one ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä the earth, ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§É (matter) ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç what is ‡§Ö‡§∏‡§§‡•ç what is not ‡§ö and ‡§Ö‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç immortal‡§ö and ‡§Ø‡§§‡•çwhat.

He¬πburns as fire; He is the sun; He is the cloud; He is Indra; He is the wind. Thisbright one is (verily) earth, matter, what¬≤ is and what¬≥ is not and also what‚Å¥is immortal.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. He burns as fire etc.‚Äî ≈öri ≈öa·πÖkarƒÅcƒÅrya explains the first half of this passage as follows:He burns as fire, shines as the sun, rains as the cloud,and rules the subjects and kills the demons as Indra.

  1. What is ‚Äî i.e., the gross, visible objects.

  2. What is not‚Äî i.e., subtle, imperceptible casualmatter. It is called asat because it is non-existent tothe senses.

  3. What is immortal‚Äî i.e,, which is the basis of therelative immortality of gods.

Here PrƒÅ·πáa is spoken of as the ruling force ofNature, nay, as Nature herself.]

‡§Ö‡§∞‡§æ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§∞‡§•‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡•å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§ã‡§ö‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ÇÍ£≥‡§∑‡§ø ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ö‡••‡•¨‡••

** ‡§∞‡§•‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡•å** in the nave of a wheel ‡§Ö‡§∞‡§æ‡§É spokes ‡§á‡§µ as‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•á in PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç all ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç are established. ‡§ã‡§ö‡§Éthe ·πöks (Veda) ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ÇÍ£≥‡§∑‡§ø Yajus (Veda) ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ø SƒÅmas(Veda) ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É Sacrifice ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç K·π£atriyas ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ BrƒÅhma·πáas ‡§öand (‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç are established in that),

As spokes in the nave of the wheel, all¬πare fixed in PrƒÅ·πáa-·πöks, Yajus, SƒÅmas, sacrifice, K·π£atriyas and BrƒÅhma·πáas.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. All are fixed in PrƒÅ·πáa etc.‚Äî Here the Vedas are mentioned as fixed in PrƒÅ·πáa inasmuch as their recitation depends upon PrƒÅ·πáa, or, it may mean that they have their original manifestation in Hira·πáyagarbha, the universal mind or PrƒÅ·πáa. PrƒÅ·πáa is identified with the universal life-force.]

** ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø ‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•á ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á‡•§ ‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§¨‡§≤‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§π‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•à‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§∏‡§ø‡••‡•≠‡••**

** ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç** thou ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§Élord of creatures (‡§∏‡§®‡•ç being) ‡§ó‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡•á in the womb ‡§ö‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø dwellest, ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•á art re-born. ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£ O PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É these ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É creatures ‡§§‡•Åagain ‡§§‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç to thee ‡§¨‡§≤‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç offerings ‡§π‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø bring, ‡§Ø‡§É that ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç thou ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•à‡§É with the PrƒÅ·πáas (i.e., senses ) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§∏‡§ødwellest.

Verily as PrajƒÅpati thou wanderest in the womb and art born again. To¬π thee, O PrƒÅ·πáa, who dwellest in the body with the senses these creatures carry their offerings.

[NOTES‚ÄîPrƒÅ·πáa is PrajƒÅpati, the universal Life; as a finite principle of life he enters into the womb and is re-born in the form of a child,-this is the play of Life, of PrƒÅ·πáa.

  1. To Thee these creatures carry etc.‚ÄîThe senses gather the perceptions of their respective objects not for any selfish gain, but for fostering the Life, the PrƒÅ·πáa in the body.]

‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡§ø ‡§µ‡§π‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Ñ‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ‡•§
‡§ã‡§∑‡•Ä‡§£‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§•‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∏‡§ø‡••‡•Æ‡••

(‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç thou) ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç for gods ‡§µ‡§π‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡§É the best carrier, ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Ñ‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç for the manes ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ first ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§ß‡§æ offering (lit. that which gives satisfaction) ‡§Ö‡§•‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ô‡•ç‡§ó‡§ø‡§∞‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•çAtharvƒÅ·πÖgiras ‡•†‡§∑‡•Ä‡§£‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç of the ·πö·π£is ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç true ‡§ö‡§∞‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç effort, work, ‡§Ö‡§∏‡§ø (thou) art.

Thou art the¬πbest carrier for gods and the first offering to the manes. Thou art the true effort of AtharvƒÅ·πÖgiras¬≤ ·πö·π£is.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. The best carrier for gods‚Äî It is believed that the god of fire, Agni, carries to other gods the oblation offered into the fire, and so he has got the name Vahni (carrier). Agni is but another expression of PrƒÅ·πáa which is immanent in all, even in the gods. So who can be a better carrier of offerings than PrƒÅ·πáa?
2. AtharvƒÅ·πÖgiras ·πö·π£is.‚Äî ≈öa·πÖkarƒÅcƒÅrya takes it as the senses.]

‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£ ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡§ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡•§
‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á ‡§ö‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡••‡•Ø‡••

** ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£** O PrƒÅ·πáa, ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç thou ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É Indra ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ by prowess ‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É Rudra ‡§Ö‡§∏‡§ø art; ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§ø‡§§‡§æ the protector ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç thou ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É the sun ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•á in the sky ‡§ö‡§∞‡§∏‡§ø movest ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç thou ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç of lights ‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É lord.

O PrƒÅ·πáa, Thou art Indra,¬π and Rudra¬≤ by prowess, and (also art Thou) the Protector.¬≥ Thou movest in the sky as the sun. Thou‚Å¥ art the lord of lights.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. Indra‚ÄîHere it may mean BrahmƒÅthe Creator.

  1. Rudra‚ÄîThe Destroyer.

  2. The Protector‚Äîi.e., Vi·π£·πáu.

  3. Thou art the lord of lights‚Äîi.e., all lights shine due to thee.]

‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡•á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£ ‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§Ü‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•¶‡••

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£ O PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç thou ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ when ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡§ø rainest ‡§Ö‡§• then ‡§§‡•á thy ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É these ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É creatures ‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø to the satisfaction of their desire ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç food ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø will be ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus ‡§Ü‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡§æ‡§É delightful ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø remain (become).

O PrƒÅ·πáa, when thou pourest down rain, these creatures of thine are delighted, hoping that there will be food according to their desire.

‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•à‡§ï‡§ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡§ø‡§É‡•§
‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•ß‡••

** ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£** O PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç thou ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Éa VrƒÅtya ‡§è‡§ï‡§ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§É the Fire named Eka·πõ·π£i.‡§∏‡§®‡•çbeing‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§æeater (enjoyer) (‡§§‡§•‡§æ likewise) ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø of the universe ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§É the good lord (or the lord of existence) (‡§Ö‡§∏‡§øthou art) ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•çwe (‡§§‡§µ thy) ‡§Ü‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø of the edible ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§É givers. ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç thou ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§®‡§É of the wind ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ father (or‚Äì‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ O MƒÅtari≈õvan ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Çthou ‡§®‡§Éours ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æfather).

Thou¬π art a VrƒÅtya O PrƒÅ·πáa, and the Eka·πõ·π£i fire that enjoys (the offerings). Thou art the universal lord of existence. We are the givers of Thy food. Thou art, O air, our father.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. Thou art a VrƒÅtya‚Äî A person is called VrƒÅtya for whom the Sa·πÅskƒÅras or the sacramental rites have not been performed, i.e., one who is ceremonially unclean. PrƒÅ·πáa being the first born there was none to perform the Sa·πÅskƒÅras for him. PrƒÅ·πÖa is called VrƒÅtya to indicate his inherent pure nature which requires no sacramental purification, and also the fact that he is the first born, the original source of the differentiated life. In Sanskrit rhetoric such expressions are called ‡§®‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§øi.e., praise in the language of blame.]

‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§®‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∑‡§ø‡•§
‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§ø ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§æ ‡§∂‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å ‡§Æ‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§É‡••‡•ß‡•®‡••

‡§§‡•á Thy ‡§Ø‡§æ which ‡§§‡§®‡•Ç‡§Ébody ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§ø in speech ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ is established ‡§Ø‡§æwhich ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•áin the ear ‡§Ø‡§æwhich ‡§öand ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∑‡§ø in the eyes (‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ is established); ‡§Ø‡§æ which ‡§ö also ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§ø in the mind ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§æ pervades, ‡§§‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç that ‡§∂‡§ø‡§µ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç propitious ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å do; ‡§Æ‡§æ do not ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§É go away.

Make propitious that¬π body of Thine which exists in speech, in the ear, in the eye, and also which pervades the mind; do not go away.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. That body of Thine‚Äî i.e., that expression of thine.

It will be explained further by the ≈öruti itself in III-5. Vide also the note on II-3.]

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§¶‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§∂‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•á ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§
‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•á‡§µ ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•á‡§π‡§ø ‡§® ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•©‡••

‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§¶‡§ø‡§µ‡•á in the three worlds ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç whatever ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç exists ‡§á‡§¶‡§Æ‡•ç this ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç all ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø of PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§µ‡§∂‡•á under the control (‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á is). ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡§æ mother ‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç the sons ‡§á‡§µ like (‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ourselves) ‡§∞‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ protect ; ‡§®‡§É for us ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Ä‡§É affluence ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç intelligence ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡•á‡§π‡§ø give. ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus.

Whatever¬πexists in the three worlds, is all under the control of PrƒÅ·πáa. (O PrƒÅ·πáa) protect us as a mother (protects) her sons; give us affluence and intelligence.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. Whatever exists etc.‚Äî≈öa·πÖkarƒÅcƒÅrya has taken the first line to mean that ‘all objects of this world are within the control of PrƒÅ·πáa and also those objects of enjoyment that are in the third heaven of Gods.’]

END OF THE SECOND QUESTION

‡§§‡•É‡§§‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§É THIRD QUESTION

** ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§π‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•å‡§∏‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•§ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§õ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á? ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§§‡•á? ‡§ï‡•á‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•á? ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á? ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡••**

‡§Ö‡§• then ‡§ö and ‡§Ü‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§≤‡§æ‡§Ø‡§®‡§É ‡§ï‡•å‡§∏‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ƒÄ≈õvalƒÅyana Kausalya ‡§è‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç him (PippalƒÅda) ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ asked, ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç Sir, ‡§è‡§∑ this ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§ï‡•Å‡§§‡§É whence ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á is born? ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç how‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç in this ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á body ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø comes? ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç how ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç himself ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø having divided ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§§‡•á exists? ‡§ï‡•á‡§® by what means ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§§‡•á goes out? ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç how ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the outside (world) ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á holds. ‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç how (‡§µ‡§æ also) ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç the internal ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus (the question).

And then ƒÄ≈õvalƒÅyana Kausalya asked him: ‚ÄòSir, whence is this PrƒÅ·πáa born? How does he come into this body, and how does he exist (there) having divided himself (into five parts)? By what means does he go out? How does he hold the outside (world), and how the¬π internal? '

[NOTES‚Äî 1. The Internal‚Äîi.e. the body, the senses, and the mind.]

** ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§∏ ‡§π‡•ã‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§∏‡§ø ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§π‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§ø‡••‡•®‡••**

‡§∏‡§É he ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à to him (Kausalya) ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö said‚Äì(‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç thou ‡§Ö‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç more difficult questions ‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§∏‡§ø) askest (‡§Ö‡§§‡§É therefore) ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§É supremely devoted to Brahman ‡§Ö‡§∏‡§ø (thou) art. ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç therefore ‡§Ö‡§π‡§Æ‡•çI ‡§§‡•á to thee ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§ø shall tell.

To him he said: ‘Thou art asking more difficult questions. Thou art the greatest devotee of Brahman, so shall I tell it to thee.

‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§® ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡•ã ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§•‡•à‡§∑‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•á ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•à‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§õ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á‡••‡•©‡••

‡§è‡§∑‡§É this ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§É from the ƒÄtman ‡§ú‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á is born. ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ as ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•á on man ‡§õ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ shadow (‡§§‡§•‡§æ so) ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç this (PrƒÅ·πáa) ‡§è‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç on this (the ƒÄtman) ‡§Ü‡§§‡§§‡§Æ‡•çis spread out, ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡•á‡§® by the act of the mind ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç in this ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á body ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø comes.

Of¬πthe ƒÄtman is born this PrƒÅ·πáa. Like the shadow on a man, it is spread out on That. It comes into the body by¬≤ the acts of the mind.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. Of the ƒÄtman is born etc.‚ÄîHere is a clear indication that the Energy whose play is the whole creation, both internal and external, is born of the ƒÄtman, and covers the Being just as a shadow spreads over a body, i.e. it has no separate existence apart from the ƒÄtman, and it shrouds the real nature of the latter under its varied display, yet it is as non-essential as a shadow. This is called MƒÅyƒÅ. It will be

  1. By the acts of the mind‚Äî i.e., according to the volitional efforts and desires of the mind. explained by the ≈öruti itself later on.]

** ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§°‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§∑ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£ ‡§á‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ï‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ó‡•á‡§µ ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡••‡•™‡••**

‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ as ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ü‡•ç the emperor ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§ø‡§ï‡•É‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç officials ‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç these ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç villages ‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç these ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç villages ‡§Ö‡§ß‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ do you reside in and rule ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•áorders, ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç so ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this (the chief PrƒÅ·πáa) ‡§á‡§§‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç other ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç PrƒÅ·πáas ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ï‡•ç ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ï‡•ç separately ‡§è‡§µ indeed ‡§∏‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§ø‡§ß‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á engages.

As an emperor orders his officials, saying ‘Do you reside in and rule these villages and those’, so does this (the chief PrƒÅ·πáa), engage the other PrƒÅ·πáas differently (in their different functions).

** ‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•á‡§Ω‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§§‡•á ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É‡•§ ‡§è‡§∑‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§∑‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•´‡••**

** ‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Ç‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡•á** (‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å-‡§â‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•) in the organs of excretion and generation ‡§Ö‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç the ApƒÅna ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ñ‡§®‡§æ‡§∏‡§ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç along with mouth and nose‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§É‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•áin the eye and the ear ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•çhimself ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§§‡•á exists. ‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á in the middle ‡§§‡•Åand ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§ÉSamƒÅna (lit. that which equalizes); ‡§π‡§øas ‡§è‡§∑‡§Éthis (SamƒÅna) ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•çthis ‡§π‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•çeaten (lit. offered) ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç food ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç equally ‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø carries (distributes). ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç from that (PrƒÅ·πáa) ‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§É these ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§∑‡§É the seven flames ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§øbecome.

The ApƒÅna is in the organs of excretion and generation; in the eye and the ear as well as in the mouth and the nose, dwells the PrƒÅ·πáa himself; and in the middle is SamƒÅna, as it distributes¬πthe offered food equally to all parts. From it originate the¬≤seven flames.

[NOTES‚Äî1. Distributes the offered food etc.‚Äîi.e., gets the food assimilated equally into the system by digestion.

  1. The seven flames‚Äîi.e., the seven organs of perception-two eyes, two ears, twoils; and the mouth.)

** ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§ï‡§∂‡§§‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§°‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∂‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§ï‡•à‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§°‡•Ä‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•¨‡••**

** ‡§è‡§∑‡§É** this ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æthe ƒÄtman ‡§π‡•É‡§¶‡§ø in the heart (‡§µ‡§∏‡§§‡§ø dwells) ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞here ‡§®‡§æ‡§°‡•Ä‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡•çof the nerves ‡§è‡§§‡§Æ‡•çthis ‡§è‡§ï‡§∂‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç hundred and one. ‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç of those ‡§è‡§ï‡•à‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç of each one ‡§∂‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§∂‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç hundred ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∂‡§æ‡§ñ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§°‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§ø in each thousand branch nerves ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§ø‡§É ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§™‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡§ø‡§É seventy-two each ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø are. ‡§Ü‡§∏‡•Å in these ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§É VyƒÅna ‡§ö‡§∞‡§§‡§ø moves.

‘In the heart dwells the ƒÄtman. There are (in the heart) a hundred-and-one nerves, in each of them there are a hundred, and each of these branch nerves again has seventy-two thousand nerves. In all these the VyƒÅna moves.

[NOTES‚Äî According to this passage, VyƒÅna is the Energy that works through the nervous system, and perhaps through arteries and veins also, during the circulation of blood. Sometimes the word ‡§®‡§æ‡§°‡•Äis translated as artery. But it is not quite correct to do so; to the ancients, the difference between artery and nerve was not known; and we find them often confusing the functions of the two as of one and the same ‡§®‡§æ‡§°‡•Ä.]

‡§Ö‡§•‡•à‡§ï‡§Ø‡•ã‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ ‡§â‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡•§
‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•á‡§® ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§Æ‡•Å‡§≠‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡••‡•≠‡••

** ‡§Ö‡§•** now ‡§â‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§É the UdƒÅna ‡§è‡§ï‡§Ø‡§æ by one (of them) ‡§ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡•ç‡§µ‡§É upwards ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§® by virtuous deeds ‡§™‡•Å‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç the virtuous world ‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø carries ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•á‡§® by sinful acts ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡§Æ‡•ç the sinful world (‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø leads); ‡§â‡§≠‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç by both ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç the human world.

‘And then, through¬π one of them the UdƒÅna carries (the soul) to the virtuous¬≤ world by virtuous deeds, to the sinful world by the sinful¬≥ acts, and by‚Å¥ both to the world of men.

[NOTES‚Äî According to this section it is the UdƒÅna Energy that carries the soul after death to the different worlds according to the good or bad Karma done by the soul in this world. Evidently then the UdƒÅna is that subtle aspect of PrƒÅ·πáa which not only pervades the whole system and sustains it but also controls the Li·πÖga≈õarƒ´ra (the subtle body) in which the soul resides after leaving the physical body.

1. Through one of them‚Äîi.e., through the Su·π£umnƒÅ NƒÅdƒ´.

2. Virtuous world‚Äîi.e., heavens of gods.

3. Sinful world‚Äîi.e., the nether worlds and such mean births as that of animals, insects, and plants.

  1. By both‚Äîi.e., when both sin and virtue are in balance state.]

** ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£ ‡§â‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑ ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§®‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§É‡•§ ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡§æ ‡§∏‡•à‡§∑‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§µ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§É‡••‡•Æ‡••**

** ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É** the sun ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à verily ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É the external ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É PrƒÅ·πáa, ‡§π‡§ø because ‡§è‡§∑‡§É it ‡§è‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç this ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç in the eye ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•É‡§π‡•ç‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡§É gracing ‡§â‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø rises. ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç of the earth ‡§Ø‡§æ which ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§§‡§æ the god (the energy) ‡§∏‡§æ that ‡§è‡§∑‡§æ this ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø of man ‡§Ö‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç ApƒÅna ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø having controlled (‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§§‡•Ä ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á exists thus favouring); ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§æ in the interspace (between heaven and earth) ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç which ‡§Ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§É the ether ‡§∏‡§É that ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É SamƒÅna, ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É the air ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§É VyƒÅna.

‘The sun is verily the external PrƒÅ·πáa,‚Äîfor he rises gracing¬πthe PrƒÅ·πáa in the eye. The^(2) god which is in the earth controls the ApƒÅna in man. The ether which is in the interspace is the SamƒÅna ; and the air is VyƒÅna.

[NOTES ‚Äî 1. Gracing the PrƒÅna in the eye. ‚Äî The rays of the sun makes the eye see.

  1. *The God which is in the earth‚Äî*Could it mean the Force of Gravity or even a vague indication of it?]

** ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡•ã ‡§π ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§â‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•Å‡§™‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•à‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•à‡§É‡••‡•Ø‡••**

** ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§É** the fire ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à verily ‡§â‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§Éthe UdƒÅna ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç therefore ‡§â‡§™‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§æ‡§É those whose fire is extinguished ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§ø in the mind ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•à‡§É absorbed ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡•à‡§É with the senses ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç rebirth (‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á attain).

‘The¬πFire is verily the UdƒÅna, for they in whom the¬≤fire is extinguished go^(3) for rebirth with their senses absorbed in the mind.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. The Fire-i.e.,‚Äî in the element fire are included both the concepts of heat and light.

    1. The fire is extinguished*‚Äîwhen the animal heat is gone.
    1. Go for rebirth etc.*‚Äîi.e., die.]

** ‡§Ø‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§∑ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø, ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡•§ ‡§∏‡§π‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•¶‡••**

** ‡§è‡§∑‡§É** this (man) (‡§Æ‡§∞‡§£‡§ï‡§æ‡§≤‡•á at the time of death) ‡§Ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§É whatever his thought (‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø becomes) ‡§§‡•á‡§® with that (thought) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç the (chief) PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡§ø comes. ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É the PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ with the Fire (UdƒÅna) ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É (‡§∏‡§®‡•ç) being united ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ the ƒÄtman ‡§∏‡§π with ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§ï‡§≤‡•ç‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç as desired ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç world ‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø leads on.
‘Whatever his thought (at the dying moment), with that he¬π comes to the PrƒÅ·πáa; the PrƒÅ·πáa united with the Fire leads on with the ƒÄtman^(2) unto the desired world.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. He comes to the PrƒÅ·πáa etc.‚Äî According to the VedƒÅnta, the self of man is encased by five

sheaths, viz. (1) Annamayako≈õa (physical sheath), (2) PrƒÅ·πáamayako≈õa (sheath of vital energy), (3) Manomayako≈õa (mental sheath), (4) VijƒÅnamayako≈õa (sheath of intellect) and (5) ƒÄnandamayako≈õa (sheath of primal nescience). These five again to go make the three bodies of man: the first forms the gross body (Sth≈´la≈õarƒ´ra), the second, third and fourth constitute the subtle body (Li·πÖga≈õarƒ´ra) and the fifth forms the causal body (KƒÅra·πáa≈õarƒ´ra). When physically alive, the soul is in all these three bodies, the causal being situated within the subtle and the subtle in the gross. In death, the self still remaining within the causal and subtle bodies separates away from the physical, and it is the subtle that forms the vehicle of the soul in its transmigration. Hence the ≈öruti tells here that after death the Jƒ´vƒÅtman comes to PrƒÅ·πáa, i.e., in the PrƒÅ·πáamayako≈õa of the subtle body with the mood of mind in which it was at the dying moment, and then moves on for a befitting reincarnation.

  1. The ƒÄtman‚ÄîThe Jƒ´vƒÅtman.]

‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•§ ‡§® ‡§π‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ ‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡§Ω‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•ß‡•• ‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§∑ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§É‚Äî

‡§Ø‡§É who ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç one who knows ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç as such ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ knows, ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø his ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ú‡§æ‡§É progeny ‡§® ‡§π never ‡§π‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á perishes, (‡§∏‡§Éhe) ‡§Ö‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§É immortal ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø becomes ; ‡§§‡§§‡•ç thus ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§É stanza :

‘The progeny of the wise man who knows the PrƒÅ·πáa as^(1)such never perishes; he becomes immortal. Here is the verse (about it).¬≤

[NOTES‚Äî 1. As such‚Äîi.e., as described before.
2. Never perishes‚Äîi.e., there never comes a break in his lineage. This might be taken as an ArthavƒÅda a mere eulogy of the Science of PrƒÅ·πáa.]

** ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•à‡§µ ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ß‡§æ‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•à‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§§ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•®‡••**

(‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É the wise) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø of the PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç origin, ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç incoming ‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç the place ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç all-perva- siveness ‡§ö ‡§è‡§µand also ‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ß‡§æfivefold (distribution); ‡§è‡§µ moreover ‡§Ö‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç internal expression ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§Ø having known ‡§Ö‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç immortality ‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡•Å‡§§‡•á attains ‡§á‡§§‡§ø so.
‘The wise attain¬π immortality having known the origin¬≤ of the PrƒÅ·πáa, its advent, place,¬≥ all-pervasiveness‚Å¥, its‚Åµ fivefold distribution, and its internal aspect,‚Äîyea, (he) attains immortality.’
[NOTES‚Äî1. Attain immortality‚Äîit may mean here the attainment of the Hira·πáyagarbha state or some powers.

    1. Origin and advent*‚Äîsee III, 3.
  1. Place‚Äîsee III, 5, 6.
    1. All*‚Äîpervasiveness‚Äîsee II, 5‚Äî13.
    1. Fivefold distribution etc*.‚Äîsee II, 3.]

END OF THE THIRD QUESTION

‡§ö‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§• ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§É FOURTH QUESTION

** ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§π‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡•Ä ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•§ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•á ‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø? ‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§ú‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø? ‡§ï‡§§‡§∞ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø? ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø? ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Å ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡••**

** ‡§Ö‡§•** then ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É of clan of Garga ‡§∏‡•å‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡•Ä the grandson of S≈´rya ‡§è‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç him (PippalƒÅda) ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ asked ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç Revered Sir, ‡§è‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç in this ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•á man ‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§ø what ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø sleep ; ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç in him ‡§ï‡§æ‡§®‡§ø what ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø are awake ‡§è‡§∑‡§É of these ‡§ï‡§§‡§∞‡§É which ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É god (sense) ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç dreams ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø see? ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø whose ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç this ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Æ‡•ç happiness ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø becomes ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç on which ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á all ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É established ‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø are?

Then GƒÅrgya SauryƒÅya·πáin asked him : ‘Revered Sir, what are they that sleep in man? and what again are awake in him? Of these which god sees dreams? whose is the happiness? on what again are all established?’

[NOTES‚ÄîThe questioner wants to know what parts of man sleep in sleep, and what are awake in the

awakened state. In sleep again what in man dream the dream, and what enjoy the calm repose of the dreamless sleep. ]

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§∏ ‡§π‡•ã‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ö‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡•ã‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§≤ ‡§è‡§ï‡•Ä‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•Å‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡•á ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§ï‡•Ä‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã ‡§® ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡§ø, ‡§® ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø, ‡§® ‡§ú‡§ø‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø, ‡§® ‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ø‡§§‡•á, ‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§∂‡§§‡•á, ‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡•á, ‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á, ‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§§‡•á, ‡§®‡•á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á, ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•á‡••‡•®‡••

‡§∏‡§É he (PippalƒÅda) ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à to him ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö said‚Äî‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ç‡§Ø O GƒÅrgya ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ as ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‡§É the setting ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø of the sun ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§É all ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§ö‡§Ø‡§É rays ‡§è‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç in this ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡•ã‡§Æ‡§£‡•ç‡§°‡§≤‡•á circle of light (solar orb) ‡§è‡§ï‡•Ä‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø become united ; ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É again ‡§â‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡§É the rising (‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø of the sun)‡§§‡§æ‡§É those (rays) ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É again ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø go out (radiate) ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç so ‡§π verily ‡§§‡§§‡•ç that ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç all (senses) ‡§™‡§∞‡•á higher ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•á in god ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§ø in mind ‡§è‡§ï‡•Ä‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø become united. ‡§§‡•á‡§® thus ‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø then ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É man (being) ‡§® ‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡§ø hears not, ‡§® ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø sees not, ‡§® ‡§ú‡§ø‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø smells not, ‡§® ‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ø‡§§‡•á tastes not, ‡§® ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•É‡§∂‡§§‡•á feels not, ‡§® ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡•á speaks not, ‡§® ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡•á takes not, ‡§® ‡§Ü‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•á enjoys not, ‡§® ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§§‡•á evacuates not, ‡§® ‡§á‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡•á moves not, (‡§§‡§¶‡§æ then) ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§ø sleeps ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus ‡§Ü‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•á says (‡§ú‡§®‡§æ‡§É man).

To him he said : ‘As the rays of the setting sun, O GƒÅrgya, become united in the orb of

light (the sun) and while rising they again go out, so (in sleep) all¬πbecome one in the superior god, the mind; hence the man hears not, sees not, smells not, tastes not, feels not, speaks not, enjoys not, evacuates not, moves not; and they say “(he) sleeps”.

[NOTES ‚Äî1. All become one etc.‚Äîi.e., all the senses and organs (both motor and sensory) become dormant in the mind.]

‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§Ø ‡§è‡§µ‡•à‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•á ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§∑‡•ã‡§Ω‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§ö‡§®‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Ø‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§π‡§µ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§É‡••‡•©‡••

‡§è‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç in this ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•á city (body) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§®‡§Ø‡§Éthe fires of PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§è‡§µ alone ‡§ú‡§æ‡§ó‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø remain awake ; ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this ‡§Ö‡§™‡§æ‡§®‡§É ApƒÅna ‡§µ‡•à verily ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É the GƒÅrhapatya fire ; ‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§®‡§É VyƒÅna ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§™‡§ö‡§®‡§É AnvƒÅhƒÅryapacana fire, ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç because ‡§ó‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§™‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç from the GƒÅrhapatya fire ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡§Ø‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç that from which it is taken ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á is taken ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£ PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§è‡§µ alone ‡§Ü‡§π‡§µ‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§É the ƒÄhavanƒ´ya fire.

‘The fires of PrƒÅ·πáa alone remain awake in this city. This Apana is the GƒÅrhapatya fire, the VyƒÅna is the AnvƒÅhƒÅryapacana and the PrƒÅ·πáa is the ƒÄhavanƒ´ya fire since it is taken from the GƒÅrhapatya fire.

[NOTES‚Äî In sleep although the senses remain dormant, the PrƒÅ·πáas ever remain active. But the significance of comparing the PrƒÅ·πáas to the fires is not very clear. In Agnihotra sacrifice, there are mainly three kinds of fires used, viz., (1) AnvƒÅhƒÅryapacana or Dak·π£inƒÅgni (2) GƒÅrhapatya and (3) ƒÄhavanƒ´ya. The first fire is placed on the southern side and is used only for offering oblations to the forefathers. The second, the household fire, is kept constantly burning on an altar and all other fires are taken from it. The third is the fire into which all the oblations to gods are offered. ≈õa·πÖkara says that as there are some similarities between the Agnis and PrƒÅ·πáas, the analogy is drawn. VyƒÅna works in the nerve on the right side of the heart; so it is compared to the Dak·π£ina fire. ApƒÅna remains active constantly in the lower part of the system. From it proceeds the PrƒÅ·πáa in sleep; so the ApƒÅna is called GƒÅrhapatya fire. And like the ƒÄhavanƒ´ya fire which is taken from the GƒÅrhapatya, PrƒÅ·πáa proceeds from ApƒÅna; so it is compared to the former fire.]

** ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§ø‡§É‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡•Å‡§§‡•Ä ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É‡•§ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ã ‡§π ‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§® ‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§´‡§≤‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡•ã‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§è‡§®‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§π‡§∞‡§π‡§∞‡•ç‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•™‡••**

‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç as ‡§è‡§§‡•å these two ‡§â‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡§®‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•å expiration andinspiration ‡§Ü‡§π‡•Å‡§§‡•Ä two oblations ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç equally ‡§®‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø takes ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus ‡§∏‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É that SamƒÅna (‡§π‡•ã‡§§‡§æ the Hot·πõ priest). ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É the mind ‡§π verily ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§É the sacrificer ‡§â‡§¶‡§æ‡§®‡§É the UdƒÅna ‡§è‡§µ indeed ‡§á‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§´‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç the fruit of the

sacrifice ‡§∏‡§É he (the UdƒÅna) ‡§è‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç this ‡§Ø‡§ú‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç the sacrificer ‡§Ö‡§π‡§∞‡§π‡§É every day ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ Brahman ‡§ó‡§Æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø takes.
As it carries the two oblations of inspiration and expiration equally into the system, the SamƒÅna is the Hot·πõ; the mind is verily the sacrificer and the UdƒÅna is the fruit of the sacrifice inasmuch as it takes the sacrificer every day to Brahman.¬π
[NOTES‚Äî 1. It takes . . . Brahman.‚ÄîOrdinarily there are three states of human consciousness‚Äî (1) the awakening state, when the physical world becomes the object of cognition, (2) the dreaming state, when dreams formed out of the impressions of the awakening state, are perceived, and (3) the state of dreamless deep sleep, when the content of consciousness is nothing of the sense world or its impressions, but a vague feeling of unconditioned being. There is a fourth state of consciousness known as SamƒÅdhi, when the consciousness of the being alone remains in its infinitude without its limiting adjuncts. The attainment of this consciousness means the realization of Brahman. The consciousness in deep sleep is very similar to this consciousness, the difference being only that the consciousness during deep sleep is vague and impermanent, while that in the latter is distinct, full of light, and permanent at least in its effect and impression. Hence the ≈öruti tells here that the UdƒÅna takes the mind, the sacrificer, every day in deep sleep to Brahman, i.e., to a state which is very near to Brahman.]

** ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§∑ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•á ‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ; ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡§ø ; ‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§¶‡§ø‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§∏‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§∏‡§ö‡•ç‡§ö, ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§É ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•´‡••**
‡§è‡§∑‡§Éthis ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É god (mind) ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ here ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•á in dream ‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç grandeur (power) ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø perceives (enjoys) ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç what ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡•ç whatever seen ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø sees again, ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§è‡§µ whatever heard ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç object ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§∂‡•É‡§£‡•ã‡§§‡§ø, hears again ‡§¶‡•á‡§∂‡§¶‡§ø‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡•à‡§É in different places and quarters ‡§ö also ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç perceived ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É again and again ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø is perceived, ‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡•ç seen ‡§ö and ‡§Ö‡§¶‡•É‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§Æ‡•ç unseen‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç heard ‡§Ö‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç unheard ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç perceived ‡§Ö‡§®‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç unperceived ‡§ö and ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç real ‡§Ö‡§∏‡§§‡•ç unreal ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç all ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø, sees (‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§™‡§ø itself) ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§É all (‡§∏‡§®‡•ç being) ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø sees.
Here, in this state, the god enjoys¬π its power of dream‚Äîit sees again whatever has been seen before, hears whatever has been heard before, enjoys again what has been enjoyed in different places and quarters. Becoming all, it sees all that has been seen and unseen, heard and unheard, perceived and unperceived real and unreal.

[NOTES‚Äî When all the senses lie dormant in sleep, the mind builds up in dream a world of its own out of the impressions received in the awakened state and enjoys the visions. All the different component parts of a dream are impressions of actual experiences, obtained, it may be, in different times; but they are curiously and fantastically linked together in sleep, when the controlling power of both reason and will is absent, and so we find that we experience things in dream which we have never seen or heard in the waking state. But ordinary dreams can be better explained physiologically than by mere psychology, although there are dream-phenomena that directly prove the existence of psychic mind and the Li·πÖga≈õarƒ´ra of man.

  1. Enjoys its power.‚Äîi.e., unlike the awakening state, enjoys its single nature untrammelled by the senses.]

** ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø, ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•à‡§∑ ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§® ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§• ‡§§‡§¶‡•à‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§û‡•ç‡§õ‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•¨‡••**

‡§∏‡§É he (the mind) ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§æ when ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§æ with the power‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§É overpowered ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø becomes ‡§Ö‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ here (in this condition) ‡§è‡§∑‡§Éthis ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§Égod (the Jƒ´vƒÅtman) ‡§∏‡•ç‡§µ‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•çthe dreams ‡§® ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø does not see. ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ then ‡§è‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á in this body ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç this ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ñ‡§Æ‡•ç bliss ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø becomes (is enjoyed).

When the mind¬π is overcome by power, the god (Jƒ´va) sees not the dream,‚Äîthen¬≤ in the body bliss is enjoyed.

[NOTES‚Äî 1.
