The mind is overcome by the power.‚Äï In the original the word is ’tejasƒÅ’ which means by ’the light’ or ‘by power.’ ≈öa·πÖkarƒÅcƒÅrya explains it as light of the sun, which is called citta and is in the nerves,’ but this does not elucidate the term. Ordinarily, the mind is conceived as a self-effulgent light lighting up everything it comes in contact with; but in deep sleep that self-effulgence of the mind is overpowered for the time being by some other power which might be of the Nature outside or of the body, and of a Tamasic kind.

  1. Then in the body etc.‚Äîi.e., the blissful, calm repose of the deep sleep, which has a ray of that beatific peace enjoyed in the super-conscious state.

** ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã‡§µ‡•É‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á, ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞ ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§§‡•á‡••‡•≠‡••**

‡§π‡•á ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Øyoung friend (lit. good-looking man) ‡§µ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ç‡§∏‡§ø the birds ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ as ‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ã‡§µ‡•É‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç the tree where they roost ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á fly towards, ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç so ‡§π verily ‡§§‡§§‡•ç that ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç all these ‡§™‡§∞‡•á in the superior ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø in the ƒÄtman ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§§‡•ágo (are established).

As birds, my young friend, go to the tree to roost, so all¬π these rest in the superior¬≤ ƒÄtman.
[NOTES‚Äî *1. All these‚Äî*i.e., what are enumerated in the next Section.

2. Superior ƒÄtman.‚Äîi.e., the Jƒ´vƒÅtman the ƒÄtman related to body etc.]

** ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä ‡§ö ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡•ã‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ö, ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡•ã‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ö, ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ö‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ö, ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§∞‡§∏‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•å ‡§ö‡§æ‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•ã‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•å ‡§ö ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§¨‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö‡§æ‡§π‡§Ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç‡§ö ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö, ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§ö‡••‡•Æ‡••**

‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä earth ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ the subtle earth element, ‡§ö also ‡§Ü‡§™‡§É ‡§ö and water ‡§Ü‡§™‡•ã‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§ö and the subtle water element, ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§Élight ‡§ö and‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡•ã‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æas the light element ‡§ö and, ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É the air ‡§ö and ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ the subtle air element ‡§ö and, ‡§Ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§É the ether ‡§ö and ‡§Ü‡§ï‡§æ‡§∂‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ the ether element ‡§öand, ‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•Å‡§Éthe eye ‡§öand ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•çobject ‡§ö and of sight, ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç the ear ‡§ö and ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the object of hearing ‡§ö and, ‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç the smell ‡§ö and ‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the object of smell ‡§ö and, ‡§∞‡§∏‡§É taste ‡§ö and ‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the object of taste ‡§ö and, ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç the touch ‡§ö and ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡•ç‡§∂‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§ö and the object of touch, ‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç speech ‡§ö and ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the object of speech ‡§öand (i.e., what can be spoken) ‡§π‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•å the two hands ‡§ö and ‡§Ü‡§¶‡§æ‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç what can be taken ‡§öand, ‡§â‡§™‡§∏‡•ç‡§•‡§Éthe organ of generation ‡§öand ‡§Ü‡§®‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the object of enjoyment ‡§ö and, ‡§™‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É

the organ of excretion ‡§ö and ‡§µ‡§ø‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the object of excretion ‡§öand, ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•åthe two feet ‡§ö and ‡§ó‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•çwhat can be walked upto, ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É the mind ‡§ö and ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the object of thought ‡§ö and, ‡§¨‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§ø‡§Éthe intellect ‡§öand ‡§¨‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the object of intellection ‡§ö and, ‡§Ö‡§π‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§É the ego ‡§ö and ‡§Ö‡§π‡§Ç‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the object of egoism ‡§öand, ‡§ö‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç the memory ‡§ö and ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the object of memory ‡§ö and, ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§É the light ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç what is to be lighted up ‡§öand, ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Éthe light PrƒÅ·πáa (Energy) ‡§öand ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ß‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç what can be held up ‡§ö and (‡§è‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•á ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á all these rest in the ƒÄtman.)

Earth and its subtle element, Water and its subtle element, Light and its subtle element, Air and its subtle element, Ether and its subtle element, the eyes and what can be seen, the smell and what can be smelt, the taste and what can be tasted, the touch and what can be touched, the organ of speech and what can be spoken, the hands and what can be taken, the organ of generation and its object of enjoyment, the organ of excretion and what can be excreted, the feet and what can be walked up to, the mind and what can be thought of, the intellect and what can be comprehended, the ego and the object of egoism, the memory and its object, the light and what

can be lighted up, the PrƒÅ·πáa and what is to be sustained‚Äîall these rest in the superior ƒÄtman in deep sleep.

[NOTES‚Äî All the gross and subtle elements with their respective senses of perception, all the organs, both motor and sensory, all intellections, even the egoity, rest unmanifested in deep sleep in the ƒÄtman. Then the Jiva remains in his KƒÅra·πáa Sarƒ´ra, vested in AvidyƒÅ alone, without the further superimposition of her ramifications or products. In this sense, deep sleep can be said to be nearer to the native glory of the ƒÄtman than even the awakening state.]

‡§è‡§∑ ‡§π‡§ø ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§æ ‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§æ ‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É‡•§ ‡§∏ ‡§™‡§∞‡•á‡§Ω‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡•á ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§§‡•á‡••‡•Ø‡••

‡§è‡§∑‡§É he ‡§π‡§ø verily ‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ the seer, ‡§∏‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡§æ he who feels ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§§‡§æ the hearer ‡§ò‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡§æ he who smells, ‡§∞‡§∏‡§Ø‡§ø‡§§‡§æ he who tastes, ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§æthe thinker, ‡§¨‡•ã‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æat the perceiver, the knower, ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§æ the doer, ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ the self of knowledge ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É the person (with all the qualifying adjuncts) ‡§∏‡§Éhe ‡§™‡§∞‡•ásupreme ‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡•áimmutable, imperishable ‡§Ü‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§øin the ƒÄtman ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§§‡•á is established.

It is he who sees, feels, hears, smells, tastes, thinks, knows; he is the doer, the intelligent soul, the Puru·π£a¬π. He¬≤ is established in the supreme immutable ƒÄtman.

[NOTES‚Äî The present section refers to the Jƒ´vƒÅtman inasmuch as the intelligence of the Jƒ´vƒÅtman makes all perception and intellection possible, the senses and the mind being only instruments through which it acts, or better, for whose existence the mind and the senses function.

    1. Puru·π£a*‚ÄîHe is called Puru·π£a because he is filled with limiting adjuncts.

2. He is established…….Supreme ƒÄtman.‚ÄîThe Jƒ´vƒÅtman stands to the ParamƒÅtman, according to the Advaita VedƒÅnta, as a portion of the sky enclosed bythe four walls of a room stands to the whole sky, or, as ≈öa·πÖkara tells in his commentary, as the myriads of sunimages reflected on different waters stand to the real The relation and division are only verbal and apparent and not real.

The Dvaitins and Vi≈õi·π£tadvaitins might take this ≈öruti as an authority for their theory of Dualism, i.e., the Jƒ´vƒÅtman and ParamƒÅtman are two different entities, the former being dependent upon the latter. But then the subsequent passages would appear hard to be reconciled to that view. Hence this passage is better explained in the Advaitic sense.]

** ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á, ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§¶‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•á; ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø, ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•¶‡•• ‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§∑ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§É‚Äî**

** ‡§Ø‡§É** who ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à assuredly ‡§§‡§§‡•ç that ‡§Ö‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the shadowless, ‡§Ö‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡§Æ‡•çbodiless, ‡§Ö‡§≤‡•ã‡§π‡§ø‡§§‡§Æ‡•çcolourless (lit. not of red colour), ‡§∂‡•Å‡§≠‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç pure ‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç indestructible ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•á

knows, ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç the supreme ‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç the indestructible ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á attains. ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø my young friend ‡§Ø‡§É ‡§§‡•Å and who again (‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç has known thus) ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É omniscient ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§É all ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø becomes, ‡§§‡§§‡•ç about that ‡§è‡§∑‡§É the following ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§É verse ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø is.

The Supreme Undecaying One, my young friend, he verily attains, who knows the indestructible, the pure, without¬π shadow, colour¬≤, or body. He becomes all and omniscient. There is the following verse about it.

[NOTES ‚Äî1. Without‚Äîi.e., unshrouded by ignorance,2. Colour‚Äîi.e., devoid of all attributes.]

‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§∏‡§π ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§∂‡•ç‡§ö ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§É
‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•§
‡§§‡§¶‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø
‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡•ß‡••

** ‡§µ‡§ø‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ** the self of intellect (Buddhi) ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡•à‡§Éall ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡•à‡§É gods (senses) ‡§∏‡§π with ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§É PrƒÅ·πáas, ‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡§ø the elements ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ in which ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø rest, ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø my friend, ‡§Ø‡§É who ‡§§‡•Å again ‡§§‡§§‡•ç that ‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç the imperishable ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ø‡§§‡•á knows ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É omniscient ‡§∏‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç all ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§Ü‡§µ‡§ø‡§µ‡•á‡§∂ enters ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus.

My young friend, he who knows that Imperishable in Which rest the mind, the senses^(1)and the PrƒÅ·πáas, verily becomes omniscient and enters into all.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. The senses and the PrƒÅ·πáas‚Äî ≈öa·πÖkarƒÅcƒÅrya explains ‘Devas’ in the text as gods like Agni, Indra, etc., who preside over the function of the senses, and PrƒÅ·πáas’ as the senses.

Enters into all‚Äîi.e., realising himself as the ƒÄtman, feels himself as existing in all.]

END OF THE FOURTH QUESTION

‡§™‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§É FIFTH QUESTION

** ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§π‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∂‡•à‡§¨‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‚Äî‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§§‡§¶‡•ç‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ã‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Ä‡§§, ‡§ï‡§§‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§µ ‡§∏ ‡§§‡•á‡§® ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§∏ ‡§π‡•ã‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡••‡•ß‡••**

‡§Ö‡§• then ‡§∂‡•à‡§¨‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ‡§É SatyakƒÅma, the son of ≈öibi ‡§è‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç him (PippalƒÅda) ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ asked, ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç Venerable Sir, ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§∑‡•Å among men, ‡§∏‡§É‡§Ø‡§Éhe who ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç until death ‡§§‡§§‡•ç that ‡§ì‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç the Om ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Ä‡§§ would meditate,. ‡§∏‡§Éhe ‡§§‡•á‡§® by that ‡§ï‡§§‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç which ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç world ‡§ú‡§Ø‡§§‡§øconquers (attains). ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à to him ‡§∏‡§É he (PippalƒÅda) ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ösaid ‡§πverily.

Then SatyakƒÅma, the son of ≈öibi, asked him, ‚ÄòVenerable Sir, among men what world does he attain by that, who would meditate upon Om until death?’ To him he replied:

‡§è‡§§‡§¶‡•ç ‡§µ‡•à ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö‡§æ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ã‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•á‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§®‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§ï‡§§‡§∞‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•®‡••

** ‡§∏‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡§æ‡§Æ** O SatyakƒÅma, ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç this ‡§µ‡•à verily ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§ö superior ‡§Ö‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§ö and inferior ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ Brahman ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç what

‡§ì‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡§É Om ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç therefore, ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç the knower ‡§è‡§§‡•á‡§® by this ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡§§‡§®‡•á‡§® means ‡§è‡§ï‡§§‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç one of the two ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø attains.

What is Om, O SatyakƒÅma, is verily the higher¬π and the lower Brahman. Therefore the knower attains either of the two by this means.

[NOTES‚Äî1. Higher and lower Brahman.‚Äîi.e., the supreme, unmanifested, absolute Brahman, and the manifested Hira·πáyagarbha.
Om being the all-comprehensive sound-symbol of Brahman, it represents the manifested state of Brahman by its audible sound, and the unmanifested by its inaudible, unexpressed form, known as the ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ß‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ or ‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§æ]

‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§ï‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Ä‡§§ ‡§∏ ‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ ‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§§‡§Æ‡•É‡§ö‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á, ‡§∏ ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡§æ ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•©‡••

** ‡§∏‡§É** he ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø if ‡§è‡§ï‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç the one syllable (i.e., A) ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Ä‡§§ meditates upon, ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§§‡•á‡§® by that ‡§è‡§µ alone ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§§‡§É being enlightened ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç quickly ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§ú‡§ó‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç into this world ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á comes back (is reborn). ‡§ã‡§ö‡§É the ·πök (ie, the first mƒÅtrƒÅ A) ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç him ‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç the world of man ‡§â‡§™‡§®‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á take. ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§∞ there ‡§§‡§™‡§∏‡§æ with Tapas (austerity) ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§£ with continence, ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§Ø‡§æ with faith ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§É being endowed ‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç greatness ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø gets.

If he meditates upon the one syllable, he comes back to this world very soon (after his death) being enlightened by that. ·πöks take him to the world of man, where he attains the greatness (in life) being endowed with austerity, continence, and faith.

‡§Ö‡§• ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§ø ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§ ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡§æ‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á‡••‡•™‡••

‡§Ö‡§• again, ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø if ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ by two syllables (A+U) (‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Ä‡§§ meditated ‡§§‡§¶‡§æ then) ‡§Æ‡§®‡§∏‡§ø in mind ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á attains (becomes united), ‡§∏‡§Éhe ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§Éby the Yajus ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç in the sky ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç the world of the moon ‡§â‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á is taken up. ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á in that world of the moon ‡§µ‡§ø‡§≠‡•Ç‡§§‡§ø‡§Æ‡•ç grandeur (objects of enjoyment) ‡§Ö‡§®‡•Å‡§≠‡•Ç‡§Ø having enjoyed ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É again ‡§Ü‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á returns.

If, again, one meditates upon the two syllables, one is united¬πwith the mind (after death). He is taken to the world of the moon in the sky, and there in that world of the moon, having enjoyed its grandeur, comes back again (into this world).

[NOTES‚Äî 1. United with the mind‚Äîi.e., remains in his ≈ö≈´k·π£ma≈õarƒ´ra, the mental body.]

‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡•å‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•á‡§®‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡•á‡§£ ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Ä‡§§ ‡§∏ ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§ø ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á ‡§∏‡§Ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§É‡•§ ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•ã‡§¶‡§∞‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§ ‡§è‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à ‡§∏ ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É ‡§∏ ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•Å‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Ç ‡§∏ ‡§è‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ú‡•ç‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§ò‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•á‡••‡•´‡•• ‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§§‡•å ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•å ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§É‚Äî

‡§Ø‡§É who ‡§™‡•Å‡§®‡§É again ‡§è‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç this (Om) ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡§£ with the three syllables (A+U+M) ‡§ì‡§Æ‡•ç Om ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus ‡§è‡§§‡•á‡§® by this ‡§Ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§∞‡•á‡§£ letter ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç the Supreme ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç Puru·π£a (Being) ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§ø‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Ä‡§§ would meditate ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§§‡•á‡§ú‡§∏‡§ø in the light ‡§∏‡•Ç‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á in the sun ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§É becomes united. ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ as ‡§™‡§æ‡§¶‡•ã‡§¶‡§∞‡§É serpent ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§ö‡§æ from the skin (slough) ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•áis freed ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç like that ‡§π ‡§µ‡•à verily ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§™‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Æ‡§®‡§æ from sins ‡§µ‡§ø‡§®‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§É becomes free. ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§É by the SƒÅma hymns ‡§â‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•Ä‡§Ø‡§§‡•á is elevated to ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç the world ofBrahmƒÅ. ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§è‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç from this ‡§ú‡•Ä‡§µ‡§ò‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç the Macrocosmic Soul (Hira·πáyagarbha) ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç the Supreme ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç existing in the heart, ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç the Puru·π£a ‡§à‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§§‡•á beholds. ‡§§‡§§‡•ç about that ‡§è‡§§‡•å these ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•å two verses ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§É are.

Again, he who meditates upon the Supreme Puru·π£a with the letter Om, constituted of three moras becomes¬πunited with the effulgent Sun. He is freed from all sins, even as a snake is freed from its slough. He is taken up to the world of BrahmƒÅ by the SƒÅma hymns. From

that Macrocosmic Self he beholds the Supreme Puru·π£a residing in the heart. There are the two following verses about it:

[NOTES‚Äî 1. Becomes united etc.‚Äîi.e., he attains the path of Kramamukti.]

‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ö‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§ ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å ‡§® ‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•á ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É‡••‡•¨‡••

‡§§‡§ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§∞‡§É the three ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ÉMƒÅtrƒÅs (moras) (‡§è‡§ï‡•à‡§ï‡§∂‡§Éseparately) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É employed (‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡•ç if) ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§Æ‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Éare mortal. ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§®‡•ç‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É when attached to one another ‡§Ö‡§®‡§µ‡§ø‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§É not wrongly employed (‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø becomes) ‡§¨‡§æ‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ß‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∏‡•Åin the external, internal, and the middle ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•Åfunctions. ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§ï‡•ç properly ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ø‡•Å‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡•Å when employed ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§É the knower ‡§® ‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç‡§™‡§§‡•ádoes not tremble.

The Three MƒÅtrƒÅs when¬π employed separately are mortal; but when¬≤ they are connected with one another, they are not wrongly employed. When¬≥ they are properly employed, in all the‚Å¥ internal, external, and middle functions, the knower trembles‚Åµ not.

[NOTES‚Äî 1. When employed separately etc.‚Äîwhen each of the three mƒÅtrƒÅs A U M, is taken separately and meditated upon, the contemplator has to be born again and again in this world as explained in V. 3. 4.

  1. When they are connected with one another etc.‚Äîi.e., when all the three ‘mƒÅtrƒÅs are blended together in significance and sound, they truly represent the universal Brahman, and when thus meditated upon, they bear the proper fruit as described in the previous section.

  2. When they are properly employed‚Äîi.e., properly meditated upon.

  3. The internal, external, and middle functions‚Äî i.e., in sleeping, waking, and dreaming states.

5.Trembles not‚Äîi.e., does not waver from the consciousness of the ƒÄtman or from the meditation.]

‡§ã‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•á‡§§‡§Ç ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡§µ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á‡•§ ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ã‡§Ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡§§‡§®‡•á‡§®‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§ø ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡§ú‡§∞‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§ö‡•á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•≠‡••

‡•†‡§ó‡•ç‡§≠‡§ø‡§Éby the ·πöks (i.e., the first mƒÅtrƒÅ) ‡§è‡§§‡§Æ‡•çthis (i.e., the world of man) ‡§Ø‡§ú‡•Å‡§≠‡§ø‡§Éby the Yajus (i.e., by the second mƒÅtrƒÅ) ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∞‡§ø‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§Æ‡•çthe sky (i.e., the world of the Moon situated in the sky) ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§Éby the SƒÅmans (i.e., by the third mƒÅtrƒÅ along with the first two) ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç what ‡§ï‡§µ‡§Ø‡§É the wise ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á know (‡§§‡§§‡•ç that ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç the world of BrahmƒÅ ‡§Ü‡§™‡•ç‡§®‡•ã‡§§‡§ø attains) ‡§Ø‡§§‡•ç what ‡§∂‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç peaceful ‡§Ö‡§ú‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç undecaying ‡§Ö‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç immortal ‡§Ö‡§≠‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç free from all fear ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•çsupreme ‡§§‡§Æ‡•çthat (Brahman) ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç the sage ‡§ì‡§ô‡•ç‡§ï‡§æ‡§∞‡•á‡§£ by Om ‡§Ü‡§Ø‡§§‡§®‡•á‡§® means ‡§è‡§µonly ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡§øgets united with. ‡§öand ‡§á‡§§‡§øthus.

By the ·πök hymns this world is attained, by Yajus the sky (the world of the moon), and by

the SƒÅmans, is attained that which is known to the wise only. What is peaceful, undecaying, immortal, free from all fear and supreme, the sage also attains by means of this Om.

[NOTES‚Äî The sound OM is produced by the combination of the three sounds A, U and M. These are the three mƒÅtrƒÅs of OM; further there is the ArdhamƒÅtrƒÅ, or the inaudible sound which still lingers even when the audible sound dies away, and which can be detected only by fine perception and concentration.

It is held that OM is the sound-symbol of Brahman, and so it is said to be the first sound produced at the beginning of creation. From the three mƒÅtrƒÅs of OM came out the ‘feet’ of GƒÅyatrƒ´, and from the three ‘feet’ came out the three Vedas and the three worlds or VyƒÅh·πõtis; From ‡§Ö came out **‘‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§∏‡§µ‡§ø‡§§‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§µ‡§∞‡•á‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç‚Äô**expanded itself into the ·πögveda, from ‡§â, ‚Äô‡§≠‡§∞‡•ç‡§ó‡•ã ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§ß‡•Ä‡§Æ‡§π‡§ø’ ’ which expanded itself into Yajurveda, and from ‡§Æ‡•ç, ‘‡§ß‡§ø‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ã‡§¶‡§Ø‡§æ‡§§‡•ç’ which expanded itself into SƒÅmaveda. The first is ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§§‡§ø‡§™‡§∞(hymnal), the second is ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§æ‡§™‡§∞ (devoted to work ), and the third is ‡§ú‡•ç‡§û‡§æ‡§®‡§™‡§∞ (devoted to knowledge).

So by the meditation upon the different mƒÅtrƒÅs different ends are attained according to the significations of the mƒÅtrƒÅs. But when the mind is concentrated upon the ArdhamƒÅtrƒÅ, the Supreme Brahman is realized. This has been indicated by the latter half of this section. For further information vide SwƒÅmi VivekƒÅnanda’s Bhaktiyoga.]

END OF THE FIFTH QUESTION

‡§∑‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§É SIXTH QUESTION

** ‡§Ö‡§• ‡§π‡•à‡§®‡§Ç ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§æ ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ú‡§É ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•§ ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç ‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§É ‡§ï‡•å‡§∏‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Å‡§™‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•à‡§§‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§§‚Äî ‡§∑‡•ã‡§°‡§∂‡§ï‡§≤‡§Ç ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ú ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§•? ‡§§‡§Æ‡§π‡§Ç ‡§ï‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§π‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§Ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§π‡§Æ‡§ø‡§Æ‡§Æ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§ï‡§•‡§Ç ‡§§‡•á ‡§®‡§æ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡§ø‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡•ã ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§è‡§∑ ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ø ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§®‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡§≠‡§ø‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•É‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç‡•§ ‡§∏ ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Ç ‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡•§ ‡§§‡§Ç ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§ï‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•å ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑? ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•ß‡••**

‡§Ö‡§• next ‡§π verily ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ú‡§É ‡§∏‡•Å‡§ï‡•á‡§∂‡§æ Suke≈õas of the BhƒÅradvƒÅja Gotra ‡§è‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç him (PippalƒÅda) ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ asked ; ‡§≠‡§ó‡§µ‡§®‡•ç holy sir, ‡§ï‡•å‡§∏‡§≤‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É of Kosala ‡§π‡§ø‡§∞‡§£‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡§É Hira·πáyanƒÅbha ‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú‡§™‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§É the prince ‡§Æ‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç me ‡§â‡§™‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø having approached ‡§è‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç this ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§∂‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç question ‡§™‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ asked : ‡§≠‡§æ‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§ú O BhƒÅradvƒÅja, ‡§∑‡•ã‡§°‡§∂‡§ï‡§≤‡§Æ‡•ç of sixteen parts ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç Puru·π£a ‡§µ‡•á‡§§‡•ç‡§• do (you) know? ‡§Ö‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç I ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç that ‡§ï‡•Å‡§Æ‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç prince ‡§Ö‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡•Å‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç said, ‡§Ö‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç I ‡§á‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç this ‡§® ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ do not know. ‡§Ö‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç I ‡§Ø‡§¶‡§ø if ‡§á‡§Æ‡§Æ‡•ç this ‡§Ö‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡§ø‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç had known (‡§§‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§ø then ) ‡§§‡•á to thee‡§ï‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç why ‡§® not ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç have told? ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus ‡§Ø‡§É who ‡§Ö‡§®‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç falsehood ‡§µ‡§¶‡§§‡§ø tells ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this one ‡§µ‡•àverily ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Ç‡§≤‡§Éwith the whole root ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§∂‡•Å‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡§ødries up (is destroyed);

‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§§‡•ç therefore ‡§Ö‡§®‡•É‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç falsehood ‡§µ‡§ï‡•ç‡§§‡•Å‡§Æ‡•ç to tell ‡§® ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§π‡§æ‡§Æ‡§øI do not deserve. ‡§∏‡§É he (the prince) ‡§§‡•Ç‡§∑‡•ç‡§£‡•Ä‡§Æ‡•ç silently ‡§∞‡§•‡§Æ‡•ç the chariot ‡§Ü‡§∞‡•Å‡§π‡•ç‡§Ø having ascended ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§µ‡§µ‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§ú went away ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§æ‡§Çto thee ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç that ‡§™‡•É‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø I ask ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•å this ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É Puru·π£a ‡§ï‡•ç‡§µwhere, ‡§á‡§§‡§øthus.

Next, Suke≈õa of the clan of BhƒÅradvƒÅja asked him: ‘Venerable Sir, Hira·πáyanƒÅbha, the prince of Kosala, came to me and put me the question, “Well BhƒÅradvƒÅja, do you know the Puru·π£a who is of sixteen parts?” I replied to the Prince, “I do not know him; had I known him, why should I not tell it to thee? He who tells a lie, perishes, root and all; so it behoves me not to tell a lie.” He got into his chariot and went away. So I ask thee where is that Puru·π£a ?’

** ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à ‡§∏ ‡§π‡•ã‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö ‡•§ ‡§á‡§π‡•à‡§µ‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§∏ ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡•ã ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡•á‡§§‡§æ‡§É ‡§∑‡•ã‡§°‡§∂‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•®‡••**

** ‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡•à** to him ‡§∏‡§É he ‡§π verily ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö said, ‡§∏‡•ã‡§Æ‡•ç‡§Ø my young friend ‡§∏‡§É that ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É the Puru·π£a ‡§á‡§π here ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É‡§∂‡§∞‡•Ä‡§∞‡•á within this body (‡§µ‡§∞‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§§‡§§‡•á exists) ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç in which ‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§É these ‡§∑‡•ã‡§°‡§∂‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ‡§É the sixteen parts ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§≠‡§µ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø arise.
To him he said: ‘Here, within this body, my friend, exists that Puru·π£a, from which arise the sixteen parts.’

[NOTE‚Äî Here it is stated that the Puru·π£a, the ƒÄtman of which more will be spoken in the subsequent sections is within this body; but the statement should not be taken in too strict a sense. As the ƒÄtman is generally perceived first as our own very self, which animates this body, it is spoken of as existing within this body. In reality He is all-pervading, unrestricted by space-limit.]

** ‡§∏ ‡§à‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á‡•§ ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§π‡§Æ‡•Å‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§ ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§µ‡§æ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡•á ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•©‡••**

‡§∏‡§É he ‡§à‡§ï‡•ç‡§∑‡§æ‡§û‡•ç‡§ö‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡•á thought ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•á who having gone out ‡§Ö‡§π‡§Æ‡•ç I (‡§Ö‡§™‡§ø also) ‡§â‡§§‡•ç‡§ï‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§Égone out ‡§≠‡§µ‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø shall become. ‡§ï‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡•á who being established ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Æ‡§ø shall be established (in this body).

He reflected: By whose going out shall I go out and by whose stay again shall I stay (in this body).

‡§∏ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§§‡•§ ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§ñ‡§Ç ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§∞‡•ç‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡§É ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É‡•§ ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§¶‡•ç‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§§‡§™‡•ã ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§É ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§É ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å ‡§ö ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ ‡§ö‡••‡•™‡••

‡§∏‡§É he (the Puru·π£a) ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§Æ‡•ç the PrƒÅ·πáa (Hira·πáyagarbha) ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§§ created. ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§£‡§æ‡§§‡•ç from the PrƒÅ·πáa ‡§∂‡•ç‡§∞‡§¶‡•ç‡§ß‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç faith ‡§ñ‡§Æ‡•ç ether, ‡§µ‡§æ‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É air, ‡§ú‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã‡§§‡§ø‡§É fire, ‡§Ü‡§™‡§É water, ‡§™‡•É‡§•‡§ø‡§µ‡•Ä earth, ‡§á‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§ø‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç the senses, ‡§Æ‡§®‡§É the mind, ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§Æ‡•ç food, ‡§Ö‡§®‡•ç‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡•ç from food ‡§µ‡•Ä‡§∞‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç vigour (strength), ‡§§‡§™‡§É penance, ‡§Æ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§É

the Vedas, ‡§ï‡§∞‡•ç‡§Æ the Yaj√±as, ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§æ‡§É the worlds, ‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡•á‡§∑‡•Å in the worlds ‡§öagain ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æname ‡§öalso (‡§Ö‡§∏‡•É‡§ú‡§§ created).

He created the PrƒÅ·πáa; from the prƒÅ·πáa came out faith¬π, ether, air, fire, water, earth, the senses, the mind, and food. From¬≤ food came vigour, penance, the Vedas, the Yaj√±as, and the worlds. And in the worlds again was created Name.

[NOTES‚Äî The sixteen categories enumerated here are the sixteen KalƒÅs or parts belonging to the Puru·π£a referred to in the previous sections. The cosmology is rather loosely described here.

  1. Faith ‚Äî ≈öraddhƒÅ is the word used in the text, and it has been explained as ƒÄstikyabuddhi, but it may very well be taken here for Buddhi itself.

  2. From Food etc.‚ÄîFood produces vigour and strength in man, which again leads him to do different works, and for the enjoyments of the results of those works different worlds were created. Hence in this sense, it has been said that ‘from food came vigour etc’.]

** ‡§∏ ‡§Ø‡§•‡•á‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§®‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§É ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø ‡§≠‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§∞‡§ø‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É ‡§∑‡•ã‡§°‡§∂‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø; ‡§≠‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Ç ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑ ‡§á‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á ‡§∏ ‡§è‡§∑‡•ã‡§Ω‡§ï‡§≤‡•ã‡§Ω‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ã ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•´‡•• ‡§§‡§¶‡•á‡§∑ ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§É‚Äî**

** ‡§∏‡§É**that ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ as ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§É coursing towards the ocean ‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§¶‡§Æ‡§æ‡§®‡§æ‡§É flowing ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É these ‡§®‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É rivers ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç the ocean ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Ø having reached ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø disappear, ‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç their ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á names and forms ‡§≠‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•á are obliterated, ‡§∏‡§Æ‡•Å‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§É the ocean ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç alone ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á is spoken of ; ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç so ‡§è‡§µ verily ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø of this ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§∞‡§∑‡•ç‡§ü‡•Å‡§É the seer of all things ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§∏‡•ç‡§Ø of the Puru·π£a, ‡§á‡§Æ‡§æ‡§É these ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§æ‡§Ø‡§£‡§æ‡§É resting in the Puru·π£a, ‡§∑‡•ã‡§°‡§∂‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ‡§É the sixteen kalƒÅs ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡•çthe Puru·π£a ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§æ‡§™‡•ç‡§Øhaving reached ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§Ç ‡§ó‡§ö‡•ç‡§õ‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§ø disappear, ‡§§‡§æ‡§∏‡§æ‡§Æ‡•ç of these ‡§®‡§æ‡§Æ‡§∞‡•Ç‡§™‡•á the name and form ‡§≠‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡•á‡§§‡•á are destroyed. ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§É the Puru·π£a. ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus ‡§è‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç alone ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡•ã‡§ö‡•ç‡§Ø‡§§‡•á is spoken of, ‡§∏‡§É that ‡§è‡§∑‡§É this (person) ‡§Ö‡§ï‡§≤‡§É devoid of KalƒÅs ‡§Ö‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡§É immortal ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø becomes ‡§§‡§§‡•ç about that ‡§è‡§∑‡§É the following ‡§∂‡•ç‡§≤‡•ã‡§ï‡§É verse ‡§≠‡§µ‡§§‡§ø is.

As the flowing rivers that tend towards the sea, having reached it, merge into the all their names and forms disappear and people speak only of the ocean, so the sixteen kalƒÅs of this Seer, the Puru·π£a, resting in Him alone, having reached Him disappear in Him; their names and forms are destroyed and people speak of the Puru·π£a only. Then He becomes devoid of kalƒÅs, and immortal. There is the following verse about it.

[NOTES‚ÄîWhen all the sixteen kalƒÅs which are cognized in the ordinary ‘ignorant’ state are merged in

the ƒÄtman in SamƒÅdhi by the practice of Yoga, then their existence is not perceived in the consciousness and the Conscious Principle, the ƒÄtman, alone remains in its unalloyed glory.]

‡§Ö‡§∞‡§æ ‡§á‡§µ ‡§∞‡§•‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡•å ‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É‡•§
‡§§‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Ç ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Ç ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§µ‡•ã ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ ‡§á‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•¨‡••

** ‡§∞‡§•‡§®‡§æ‡§≠‡•å** in the nave of the chariot ‡§Ö‡§∞‡§æ‡§É spokes ‡§á‡§µ like ‡§ï‡§≤‡§æ‡§É the KalƒÅs ‡§Ø‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§ø‡§®‡•ç in whom ‡§™‡•ç‡§∞‡§§‡§ø‡§∑‡•ç‡§†‡§ø‡§§‡§æ‡§É are established ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç that ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§Æ‡•ç worth knowing ‡§™‡•Å‡§∞‡•Å‡§∑‡§Æ‡•ç the Puru·π£a ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ know ‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ so that ‡§Æ‡•É‡§§‡•ç‡§Ø‡•Å‡§É death‡§µ‡§É ye ‡§Æ‡§æ ‡§™‡§∞‡§ø‡§µ‡•ç‡§Ø‡§•‡§æ‡§É may not hurt.

In whom rest the kalƒÅs like spokes in the nave of a chariot-wheel, know Him, the Puru·π£a, worthy to be known, that death might not hurt you.

[NOTE‚ÄîThe simile given here is very significant. As the spokes only rest on the nave but do not form an integral part of the same, so these kalƒÅs are not part of the Puru·π£a in the real sense of the term; they are mere erections of His MƒÅyƒÅ≈õakti, and as such, are dependent on Him.]

** ‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç ‡§π‡•ã‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö‡•à‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§¶‡•á‡§µ‡§æ‡§π‡§Æ‡•á‡§§‡§§‡•ç ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶‡•§ ‡§®‡§æ‡§§‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡••‡•≠‡••**

‡§§‡§æ‡§®‡•ç to them (‡§∏‡§É he) ‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö said, ‡§Ö‡§π‡§Æ‡•çI ‡§è‡§§‡§æ‡§µ‡§§‡•ç up to this ‡§è‡§§‡§§‡•ç this ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç Supreme ‡§¨‡•ç‡§∞‡§π‡•ç‡§Æ the Brahman ‡§µ‡•á‡§¶ know. ‡§Ö‡§§‡§É beyond this ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç suprerior ‡§® ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡§ø there is not.

To them he said, ‘So far I know of the Supreme Brahman; there is nothing higher than that.’

** ‡§§‡•á ‡§§‡§Æ‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§∏‡•ç‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Ç ‡§π‡§ø ‡§®‡§É ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ ‡§Ø‡•ã‡§Ω‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡§Æ‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ç ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§∏‡•Ä‡§§‡§ø‡•§ ‡§®‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡•ã ‡§®‡§Æ‡§É ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É‡••**

** ‡§§‡•á** they (the six questioners) ‡§§‡§Æ‡•ç him ‡§Ö‡§∞‡•ç‡§ö‡§Ø‡§®‡•ç‡§§‡§É having worshipped (‡§â‡§µ‡§æ‡§ö said ) ‡§§‡•ç‡§µ‡§Æ‡•ç ‡§π‡§ø verily thou (art) ‡§®‡§É our ‡§™‡§ø‡§§‡§æ father, ‡§Ø‡§É who ‡§Ö‡§∏‡•ç‡§Æ‡§æ‡§ï‡§Æ‡•ç us ‡§Ö‡§µ‡§ø‡§¶‡•ç‡§Ø‡§æ‡§Ø‡§æ‡§É of the ignorance ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç the supreme ‡§™‡§æ‡§∞‡§Æ‡•ç the shore across ‡§§‡§æ‡§∞‡§Ø‡§∏‡§ø taken ‡§á‡§§‡§ø thus, ‡§®‡§Æ‡§É Obeisance ‡§™‡§∞‡§Æ‡§ã‡§∑‡§ø‡§≠‡•ç‡§Ø‡§É to the highest ·πö·π£is.

Having worshipped him, they said, ‘Thou art our father that hast taken us across the other shore of avidyƒÅ (ignorance).’

Obeisance to the highest ·πö·π£is!
Obeisance to the highest ·πö·π£is!

END OF THE SIXTH QUESTION
